Issue of Agencies Handling Communist Cases

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice states that military tribunals are in the process of being abolished. Regarding the handling of Communist cases, except for those already adjudicated, they will be handled as usual. Those not yet concluded should be transferred to the Higher Courts of the respective provinces, and those courts should investigate the circumstances of the crimes and determine jurisdiction accordingly. However, if the crime was committed in an area that is under martial law or is an area for bandit suppression, it can be sent to the military commander or court of that area for trial. But, if the location of the Higher Court is currently in a martial law area, it may be transferred to the highest military authority in that location for handling. If there is no martial law or bandit suppression in the respective provinces, the receiving Higher Court will continue the trial. Hereafter, Communist cases will be handled accordingly. (Special dispatch, 10th)

New Italian Envoy Arrives in Nanjing

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Italian Ambassador to China, Pellegrino Ghigi, arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai at 7:00 AM on the 10th, accompanied by Secretary Zanetti. Five Ministries Confer on National Coal Relief; Ministry of Industry Proposes Seven Proposals

(Nanjing) In the afternoon of the 10th, the Ministry of Industry invited representatives from the Ministries of Finance, Foreign Affairs, Military Affairs, Transportation, and Railways to hold a joint meeting to discuss ways to relieve the national coal industry and resist foreign coal. Liu Jichi chaired the meeting, reporting on the situation of foreign coal dumping and the current state of the national coal industry's decline. He then presented the Ministry of Industry's seven proposed relief measures: (1) Implement strict tariff protection policies and levy dumping duties on foreign coal; (2) Reduce costs (such as operating expenses, start-up costs, mine-to-station transportation costs, loading and unloading fees, dock fees, etc.); (3) Improve transportation routes to ensure an adequate supply of coal-carrying vehicles; (4) Seek unity among the various coal mining industries to strengthen self-reliance; (5) Eliminate monopolistic practices by mine owners; (6) Exempt illegal levies and reduce mineral taxes; (7) Reduce railway and shipping freight rates, etc. The proposals were submitted for deliberation. After three hours of study by the representatives, it was felt that the issue was significant and no decision was made lightly. It was decided that each representative would consult with their respective ministers, and each ministry would submit its opinions for discussion at the meeting on the 24th, for a final decision. (Special dispatch, 10th)

Han Fuqu Rectifies Officialdom in Linyi

(Jinan) Han Fuqu is still in Linyi today. Because many people complained about the district chiefs, the chiefs of the fifth, sixth, and seventh districts were removed. Han is waiting for the arrival of Wu Zhenzan, the president of the High Court, to clear up the backlog of cases before going to Feixian. (Special dispatch, 10th)

Current Commentary

League of Nations Declares Non-Recognition of Puppet Organizations

— Yuan

On June 14th of this year, the State Council, in the name of the Advisory Committee, proposed a plan regarding the non-recognition of the puppet state of Manchukuo. It circulated this plan to member and non-member states of the League of Nations, and also sent letters to the representatives of the eighteen nations on the committee, stating that if no objection was received, the plan would be considered established. Now, according to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, ten replies have been received, all expressing support. The United States, in its reply, indicated that if the puppet organization requests to join any international treaties, such as the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the U.S. government will not give it any attention. Britain, pointing out the omission of the two conventions on maritime safety and load lines in the notification, insisted on joining, making its attitude of non-recognition very clear and resolute. Other small countries, such as Cuba, Venezuela, Haiti, Colombia, and Nicaragua, also generally acknowledged the principle, but were still considering the listed items. Only Siam showed slight hesitation, but only stated that it had no relationship with Manchuria and did not express opposition. It can be seen that the world's nations are clearly and unanimously against the puppet state of Manchukuo. The reason why the world's nations unanimously deny the puppet state of Manchukuo is that the puppet state of Manchukuo was created by Japanese aggression, seizing Chinese land to place it under another power, destroying Chinese territory, which is undeniable. Now the League of Nations' non-recognition of the puppet state essentially recognizes that the land of the puppet state of Manchukuo belongs to China, to express its intention to protect the territorial integrity of its member states. Although it cannot go so far as to sanction Japan with force, this fair claim can still impose some restraint on those who rely on force. On the one hand, it can make the Chinese people aware that justice still exists in the world. Since the world's nations do not recognize the puppet state of Manchukuo, it means that Manchurian territory has not yet reached a point of no return due to accommodating established facts. There is still a glimmer of hope left for our people to strive for. Our people, if they are not insane, will increase their belief in recovering lost territory. Our national strength may be weak, but the desire to recover lost territory has never been forgotten. How can it be that the world's nations sympathize with us in not recognizing a puppet organization created by force, while our people would bow down and accept it? This is what we dare to resolutely express in accepting the League of Nations' good intentions.

However, the League of Nations' Opium Advisory Committee's handling of this issue is very puzzling to us. Yesterday, the Kuomin News Agency reported that today's decision on the report would refer to any places involving the Manchukuo puppet organization as "Manchuria and Jehol, also known as 'Manchukuo'," etc. This technical naming is due to the fact that the committee members, after Secretary-General Drummond announced last night that major countries almost unanimously advocated maintaining a policy of non-recognition of the puppet organization, decided on it. This ambiguous and skillfully evasive resolution has already made us suspicious. According to today's Havas News Agency report, the Japanese representative, Yokoyama, requested that the name of Manchuria and Jehol in the report be annotated with the words "i.e., the territory of the so-called 'Manchukuo'." After review by the legal department, it was approved. This is even more bizarre. As mentioned earlier, using technical naming already violates the League of Nations' impartial attitude. If, as today's Havas report says, the annotation "territory of the so-called 'Manchukuo'" is added at the request of Japan, it shows a contradiction with the policy of major countries unanimously advocating maintaining non-recognition of the puppet organization. It also contradicts the US reply, which stated that it would never pay attention if the puppet organization requested to join any international treaty. Even if the Japanese have sophisticated diplomatic tactics, combining inducement and coercion, how could the legal department dare to rashly bear the responsibility of undermining the League of Nations' unified policy? If the news reported by Havas is accurate, we know that the League of Nations will definitely find a way to salvage it and eliminate the stain of its self-contradiction and internal inconsistency.

League of Nations Advisory Committee Passes Opium Report; Danger of Secret Drug-Making Plants in the Far East

(Geneva) Today, the Opium Advisory Committee passed a report on the illegal trade in narcotics, which explicitly stated the danger of secret drug-making plants in China and the Far East and drew attention to the increasing amount of high-concentration opium imported into India from the Far East in recent years. (Reuters dispatch, 9th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Advisory Committee on Opium Issues passed a report containing the following points: (1) Illegal trafficking; (2) Cooperation between Chinese authorities and authorities in the concessions; (3) Supervision of opium and narcotic drug trafficking in Manchuria and Jehol; (4) Various issues related to the 1931 Convention for Limiting the Manufacture and Regulating the Distribution of Narcotic Drugs; (5) Bangkok Conference and Convention; (6) Organization of the Advisory Committee, etc. Japanese delegate Yokoyama requested that the name "Manchuria and Jehol" in the report be annotated with the words "i.e., the territory of the so-called 'Manchukuo'." After review by the legal department, it was approved. The report to be submitted by the Opium Advisory Committee to the League of Nations will briefly explain the work of the 17th session of the Committee, which opened on October 30 and closed today. Regarding the issue of confiscation, the subcommittee will hold a meeting before the Advisory Committee meeting to review various reports and other documents related to illegal trafficking. The report of the Advisory Committee on Opium Issues requests the League of Nations Executive Council to pay attention to the following points: (1) Various small factories secretly manufacturing narcotics all over the world; (2) High-concentration opium illegally transported from the Far East to India, which had decreased at some point, has now increased again; (3) Narcotics secretly transported from ports in Europe and the Far East to the United States; (4) New methods used by illegal traffickers to avoid inspection. The US representative made an important declaration to the Committee regarding private trafficking, stating that some people are using private aircraft to smuggle alcoholic beverages and narcotics into major North American countries. The report also stated that attention should be paid to the use of international sleeping cars for smuggling narcotics. The committee does not advocate listing the names of merchants who privately traffic in narcotics, but requests the committee's secretary to supplement the index contained in the report of the detention agency at any time. This index contains the names of the most important and well-known private traffickers, as well as their relationship to a certain smuggling case. Regarding the issue of cooperation between Chinese authorities and treaty countries, the committee believes that supplementary investigations are necessary regarding legislative events and the difficulties encountered by various agencies. The committee also believes that it is necessary to encourage Chinese authorities and foreign representatives in China to exchange information. The committee paid particular attention to the fact that the authorities of the so-called "Manchukuo" have adopted and promulgated various measures, the result of which will make opium a monopoly. The "Manchukuo" authorities are using this to increase important revenue. The committee received reports proving that the policies implemented by "Manchukuo" not only increase drug addiction in Manchuria and Jehol but will also endanger other countries. The report also requested that major producing and manufacturing countries closely monitor requests for the transportation of narcotics to Manchuria and Jehol. Finally, the committee also suggested that Turkey, Canada, and a certain country in the Scandinavian Peninsula participate in the Advisory Committee and requested the Executive Council to approve it. Before adjourning the meeting, the Advisory Committee expressed regret over the withdrawal of the German representative, saying that Germany's position is extremely important in terms of manufacturing and commerce, and its departure has a great impact on the success or failure of the Advisory Committee's work. It is hoped that the country will soon be able to participate in cooperation again, and the vacancy left by its representative will not be filled for the time being. (Havas dispatch, 9th)

Japanese Policy Towards China Follows Decisions Made at the Five-Minister Conference

(Tokyo) During today's cabinet meeting, some officials raised questions about the situation of the Nanjing government. Foreign Minister Hirota replied that no matter what measures the Nanjing government takes, the Japanese government must base its steps on the fundamental policy decided at the Five-Minister Conference. (Domei News Agency dispatch, 10th)

Soviet Russia Announces Protest Note to Japan Regarding Japanese Aircraft Intrusion into Russian Airspace; States that This Act is Unprecedentedly Violent, Demanding Guarantees for the Future and Punishment of Those Responsible

(Moscow) Since the Soviet Russian government denounced Japanese military aircraft for flying into Russian territory and violating territorial rights, relations between the two countries have become increasingly distant. There is clear evidence today. The Soviet Russian ambassador to Japan's protest note to the Japanese Foreign Ministry regarding the aircraft trespassing incident was also released by the Russian government today. The wording in the note is strong, claiming that this act is an unprecedented violation of Soviet Russian territory, which shows the Russian side's emphasis on this matter. According to political sources, at the Soviet Russian celebration of the 16th anniversary of the Communist Revolution the day before, ambassadors from various countries participated in the grand ceremony, but Japanese Ambassador Ota did not attend the parade. In the evening, when Soviet Russian Central Executive Committee Chairman Kalinin formally received congratulations, Ota did not go either. This situation, as well as the fierce speech by Soviet Russian People's Committee Chairman Molotov on that day, has aroused much commentary. It is generally believed that there has been little progress in relations between the two countries. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch, 9th)

(Nanjing) Soviet Ambassador to Japan Yurenev, on the orders of the Soviet government, submitted a protest to Foreign Minister Hirota on November 6 regarding Japanese military aircraft flying into Soviet territory. The memorandum pointed out that on November 3, eight Japanese reconnaissance planes and one bomber flew to the vicinity of Slavjanka and Barabash on the west coast of Amur Bay. Japanese military aircraft flew over numerous locations within Soviet territory, 25 to 30 kilometers from the border. The memorandum further stated, "I am authorized by the Soviet government to protest against this violent and unprecedented intrusion into the Soviet border, and insist that such actions not occur again in the future. A thorough investigation of the truth of this incident must be conducted, and the aforementioned flight personnel must be punished." The conclusion stated, "I wish to express my firm belief that the Japanese government will be able to take effective steps to satisfy this statement." (TASS dispatch, 8th)

Japanese Foreign Ministry States that a Russian-Japanese War Would be Unfavorable to Both Sides; Believes There Is a Need to Ease the Atmosphere

(Tokyo) At a time when the resumption of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia is about to be realized, the Soviet Russian side issued a warning to Japan, saying that Japanese aircraft flying into the Primorsky Krai region without authorization will lead to unpleasant consequences. The Japanese Foreign Ministry released the following views last night: There are currently no disputes between Japan and Russia that would trigger a crisis of war. Moreover, a Russian-Japanese war would be unfavorable to both countries. From a historical and experimental point of view, it is true that small matters can disrupt the situation. Therefore, it is necessary for the Japanese and Russian authorities to find ways to improve the atmosphere between Japan and Russia. Regarding this point, Foreign Minister Hirota warned Ambassador Yurenev, but Soviet Russia is still repeatedly engaging in anti-Japanese propaganda, which is unreasonable. If peace between Japan and Russia is disrupted, the responsibility lies with Soviet Russia. Japan welcomes the resumption of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia from the perspective of world peace and human well-being. It is incomprehensible that this goodwill and tolerance are used to launch anti-Japanese propaganda as a tool of international diplomacy. We cannot help but be disappointed by such narrow and short-sighted policies on the part of the Soviet Russian authorities. Regarding the current issue of Japanese military aircraft, Soviet Russia believes that the United States is most concerned about the Japanese military's strategy to conquer the Primorsky Krai, so it is using this point to engage in counter-propaganda, hoping to benefit the resumption of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia. However, Japan has absolutely no such facts, and can ignore it. (Dentsu dispatch, 10th)

Japanese Newspaper Reports Rebellion of Red Army Villagers Along Ussuri Railway; Sixteen Aircraft Burned

(Tokyo) The Tokyo Jiji Shinbun reported that villagers and Red Army soldiers near Vyazemskaya along the Ussuri Railway have rebelled, and their momentum is growing. The Red Guards along the Ussuri Railway are also stirring. It is reported that the rebels have massacred hundreds of Communists and burned sixteen military aircraft. The leader of the rebels flew an aircraft to distribute leaflets, urging the people to respond, but was shot down by government forces. The unrest has a tendency to spread, but officialdom has not yet received any real news. Someone inquired at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs about the source of this news. It is said that it came from a certain Russian newspaper in Harbin and was spread as an extra edition. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

Indian-Japanese Conference Suffers Another Setback

Delhi The final, eleventh plenary session of the Japanese-Indian conference, slightly delayed from the scheduled time, convened at 5:00 PM today. Based on the government's final instructions, the Japanese representatives put forward the following final proposal: (1) The standard for the quantity of Indian cotton purchased is one million bales. Abolish the fixed system. For each additional bale, increase cotton cloth by 200 yards. The maximum quantity of Indian cotton purchased is 1,375,000 bales, and the quantity of cotton cloth exported is 400 million yards; (2) Although Japan opposes the classification of cotton cloth by variety, considering India's position, it acknowledges mutual flexibility. Unprocessed goods account for 45%, and cloth other than processed goods accounts for 55%. The numbers in this proposal by the Japanese side are based on the actual performance of Japanese cotton cloth imports from last year to the seventh year in the trade statistics investigated by the Indian Ministry of Commerce. India did not state any opinions on this, replying that it would consult with Indian operators before answering again. The meeting adjourned at 5:50 PM. The negotiations, which were expected to be the last, suffered another setback due to India's uncooperative attitude. (Dentsu News Agency dispatch, 9th)

French Parliament Questions Government's Foreign Policy; Leaning Towards Japan Will Cause Dissatisfaction with the United States; What Attitude to Take in a Japanese-American Conflict

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies convened at 9:40 AM, chaired by Speaker Herriot, to continue presenting questions on foreign policy. Tedinri, a deputy from Paris belonging to the Republican League, took the stage to question the attitude adopted by the French government to maintain European peace after Germany decided to withdraw from Geneva. Macaigne, a deputy from the Radical Socialist Republican Party, then took the stage to question the government's foreign policy, saying, "If we lean towards Japan, we will inevitably cause dissatisfaction with the United States. In the London Economic Conference, we overemphasized currency and neglected economic issues." Macaigne recounted the difficulties encountered by President Roosevelt's economic and financial policies, saying that in order to solve the consumption problem, it is necessary for mutual understanding between the various nations. However, the French Foreign Ministry does not have time to take care of the situation in the East, which is a pity. In the East, there are one billion residents, and if their consumption capacity increases, the French export industry will definitely benefit from it. Finally, Macaigne questioned, if France is attacked by Germany, which countries can be France's arms? He also said, what point of view will France take when conflicts arise between China, Japan, and the United States in the future? At this point, the Speaker announced that the discussion would be postponed until 3:30 PM. The meeting adjourned at 12:30 PM. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Resumption of Diplomatic Relations Between the US and Russia Imminent; Litvinov and Hull Meet for the Second Time; Diplomatic and Commercial Matters Largely Agreed; Awaiting Roosevelt's Final Decision

(Washington) The complete restoration of diplomatic and commercial relations between the United States and Russia is now expected to be announced by the White House after a formal meeting between the US President and Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov tomorrow afternoon. Litvinov was originally scheduled to meet with the President at 5:00 PM this afternoon, but it was postponed by one day because some issues had not yet been agreed upon. However, it is heard that these issues are not difficult. Litvinov also held talks with US Secretary of State Hull at the State Department for two hours today. This was the second conversation between the two, but government officials expect that all issues can be resolved before the President receives Litvinov tomorrow. The US market has been hoping for a statement on the resumption of diplomatic relations for three days. It is said that if the meeting unfortunately breaks down, the entire pharmaceutical and financial community will be greatly disappointed, because the business community expects that after the resumption of diplomatic relations, a trade agreement can be established, allowing American manufactured goods and some agricultural products to gain a large market in the Soviet Russian market. (Kuomin News Agency dispatch, 9th)

(Washington) Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov and US Secretary of State Hull met for two hours today and have agreed on the basis of understanding regarding diplomatic and economic relations between the two countries, which will be submitted to President Roosevelt for approval this afternoon. (Reuters dispatch, 9th)

Talk Delayed; Provokes Speculation

(Washington) The White House and the State Department are absolutely silent on the reason for the delay in the talks between President Roosevelt and Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov. The newspapers also have no explanation for this. The New York Times said that the details of the talks are not disclosed, indicating that differences may have arisen between the views of the US and Russian governments. The Ming Sheng Jiang Tan Bao also does not deny the possibility of differences between the views of the two countries. Some sources said that Undersecretary of State Bullitt will be appointed as the US Ambassador to the Soviet Union, while others said that Henry Morgenthau, President of the Farm Credit Administration, will be appointed. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

White House Banquet; Toasts and Merriment

(Washington) On November 8, Litvinov met with US Secretary of State Hull and held talks for more than two hours. At the end of the meeting, Hull led Litvinov to a gathering of journalists. Litvinov made a brief statement, saying, "I am very pleased in Washington, because I have found a friendly atmosphere here that supports my mission to the United States." Hull and Litvinov subsequently issued a joint statement, stating, "We have conducted very friendly and private discussions on a number of issues regarding Soviet relations. These talks are purely preliminary and have not discussed detailed proposals." After that, Roosevelt held a banquet at the White House to entertain the guests, including Litvinov, Soviet Intelligence Director in Washington Svirski, Manager of the US Company Tangdanov, Secretary of the Soviet Foreign Ministry Dievierkovski, Director of the Intelligence Department of the Committee Umanjski, the US Secretary of State, the Minister of Agriculture, the Minister of the Interior, the Minister of Commerce, and other important officials of the US government. Litvinov then went to the State Department to continue talks with Hull. This talk continued on the 9th, and Litvinov met with Roosevelt again at 6:00 PM in the evening. (TASS dispatch, 9th)

Two Treaties; Conclude Negotiations

(Washington) The US-Russian negotiations will roughly conclude with two treaties, one being a treaty of political and economic non-aggression, and the other being a treaty defining aggressor countries. According to this treaty, "any country that sends troops to a country outside its own territory is an aggressor." There is originally no danger of war between the US and Russia, but those responsible for mediating the two countries cannot but guard against the danger of economic conflict between the two sides. (Havas dispatch, 9th)

The Reason Gonorrhea is Difficult to Treat

The difficulty of treating gonorrhea is a common cry from both the medical community and patients. There are many reasons why gonorrhea is difficult to treat. First, after the acute symptoms of gonorrhea have passed and it becomes chronic, the patient no longer experiences severe pain and is unwilling to continue treatment to eradicate the disease. This is because the patient lacks the patience. Second, the patient does not understand the methods of self-care, such as sexual activity, alcohol consumption, overwork, etc., all of which prolong the duration of gonorrhea treatment. Third, there is the issue of finances; there is no money for treatment. However, from our medical perspective, the most significant reason gonorrhea is difficult to treat, aside from the reasons mentioned above, is due to the anatomical structure of the urethra. The urethra has many mucous glands along its path, such as Littre's glands, Cowper's glands, and the prostate gland, all of which open into the urethra. Physicians can use antibacterial drugs to kill the gonococci in the urethra, but it is difficult to kill the gonococci lurking within these glands. Therefore, gonorrhea that appears to be cured on the surface can recur when exposed to various triggering factors such as fatigue, sexual activity, and alcohol consumption. This is because the gonococci lurking within the glands emerge and cause trouble again. Therefore, to eradicate gonorrhea, an experienced physician must use a new deep sterilization technique to treat these gonococcal nests properly, only then can it be eradicated!

Taverns asked their customers to order food before one o'clock in the afternoon so that all work would be stopped at one o'clock. Afterwards, the urn containing Katayama's ashes was placed inside the Kremlin wall, and cannons were fired in mourning.

Beck praised Katayama's tasks in the international labor movement. The next speaker was Marti, who vigorously stated that Katayama was a resolute enemy of Japanese imperialism to the death. Marti pointed out that Katayama used extremely sharp words to expose the true nature of the Japanese army's occupation of Manchuria, and indicated that the creation of "Manchukuo" was merely an excuse, a mask, to cover up the Japanese imperialism's specially planned military preparations to attack the Soviet Union. Then, Okin, the representative of the Japanese Communist Party, described the life of this deceased revolutionary in vivid words, and his courageous and uncompromising struggle to win the Japanese people's solution. He said, "The Japanese military clique headed by Araki is preparing to attack the Soviet Union, and Katayama left us a mortal struggle to oppose Japanese imperialism, oppose patriotism, strive for the liberation of Korea, Taiwan, and China from their oppressors, strive for the liberation of the entire oppressed Eastern working masses, and always maintain a united friendship with the Soviet Union. Katayama also left us with loyalty to the Soviet Union, and a relentless struggle against imperialist provocations and counter-revolutionary imperialist wars. If Japanese imperialism is truly going to point its bloody hand at the Soviet Union, we vow to transform this war into a civil war, into a war to liberate the Japanese working masses and the oppressed colonial people from the brutal rule of Japanese capitalists and landlords, and to overthrow the hegemony of the Japanese autocratic military clique." Wang Ming (transliteration), the representative of the Chinese Communist Party, spoke next, and the meeting ended. Then, Stalin, Molotov, and others carried the ash box to the Kremlin and placed it inside the wall. After cannons were fired in salute, the magnificent procession of Moscow workers passed through Red Square to pay their last respects to this communist leader. (TASS, 10th)

Conflict Between Postal Workers and Station Police at Beijing Railway Station; Many Seriously Injured on Both Sides

(Nanjing) At 7:00 AM on the 10th, when the No. 6 train from Shanghai arrived at the station, postal unloading workers were still entering and exiting through the south gate. Station police squad leader Li Junhai and others negotiated with them, but the workers refused to obey instructions, leading to an argument and then a violent fight. While they were arguing, Police Chief Huang Liang led a second batch of police and immediately tied up nine workers, injuring two. Those who escaped called for help, and members of other gangs, their families, and onlookers, numbering several thousand, surrounded the Great King Temple. It was dark, and only three or five gunshots and a chorus of cries were heard. Later, after mediation by District Chief Xiao Jie and others, the police released the nine bound workers to the union for punishment. Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway to Hold Full Line Opening Ceremony

(Hangzhou) The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, the largest construction project in Zhejiang Province, has been under construction since 1929 when Zhang Jingjiang, the former chairman of Zhejiang Province, began raising funds. In June of that year, the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Engineering Bureau was established, with Du Zhenyuan in charge. After years of operation, the entire line will be completed by the end of this month. According to Tan, the chief of the general affairs section of the bureau, the total cost of completing the entire line is 14 million yuan. The current operating income of the completed sections is approximately 120,000 yuan per month. After deducting expenses of approximately 80,000 yuan, there is a monthly surplus of 40,000 yuan. After the entire line is opened, it will definitely be more developed. The railway has now been completed to Jiangshan. The entire line is scheduled to be completed by the end of the month. It is planned to hold a full-line trial run next month and a full-line opening ceremony in Jinhua on the 25th or 28th of next month. At that time, invitations will be sent to the Minister of Railways, important party and government figures, and foreign guests to participate in the grand ceremony. (Central News Agency, 10th)

Ancient Zeng State Tomb Discovered in Ancient Yin Dynasty Village; Spring and Autumn Culture Can Be Studied Here; Another Remarkable Discovery in Archaeological Work in Southern Shandong

Jinan Dispatch. The Shandong Ancient Sites Research Association, jointly established by the Academia Sinica and the Shandong Provincial Government, has been excavating the ancient capital sites of the Shang, Zhou, Spring and Autumn, and Warring States periods in the three counties of Zou, Teng, and Yi in southern Shandong. Since work began on the Cao Wang tomb in Anshang Village, Teng County, many remarkable discoveries have been made, attracting significant attention from various places. Recently, near the ancient Yin Dynasty village of Egukou, 30 miles north of Yi County, the ancient site of the ancient Zeng State tomb from the Spring and Autumn period was discovered. According to a long-distance telephone report from the Yi County Magistrate: Yi County was the land of the Zeng State during the Spring and Autumn period. The State of Chu established the Lanling Town here, and the State of Jin established the Lanling Prefecture. In the Jin dynasty, it was established as Yi Prefecture, and it was changed to a county only after the Ming Dynasty. The Zeng State appears to be the surname. During the Spring and Autumn period, it was destroyed by the State of Ju. Therefore, the history of Yi County is quite long. Egukou Village, thirty miles north of the city, is said to be an ancient Yin Dynasty village, with records to prove it. Broken bricks, tiles, and porcelain shards are everywhere outside the village, with an ancient feel and evident remains. About two miles west of the village is Xiaoguojiazhuang, where two ancient tombs were recently discovered, having collapsed from the ground. The ground cave is about five feet deep. Inside the cave, a stone house opens eastward, with huge stones inlaid on the outside. The door is supported by a bluestone beam about ten feet long, decorated with lotus flowers, elegant and refined. The interior is dark, and no one dares to enter. A pole several feet long was used to probe, but there were no boundaries. Another tomb is located half a mile southwest of this tomb, in a barren mountain area, with the same shape. At present, the easternmost one has been covered with huge stones and soil by the landowner because it interfered with farming, and it cannot be seen again. According to the identification of archaeologists on these ancient tombs, it has been confirmed that they are Zeng State tombs. Although they have not yet been excavated, the external observation is sufficient to express the greatness and exquisiteness of ancient architectural art. It is likely that these ancient tombs are by no means owned by ordinary people, or they may be related to the imperial family. At present, the residents of the village have sent a letter to the Yi County Party Headquarters. Upon receiving the report, Yan Yudong, a member of the Standing Committee of the County Party Headquarters, personally went to investigate. Considering that the matter concerns ancient cultural relics, he has sent a letter to the Yi County Government, requesting permission to excavate, collect, and preserve the relics. It is expected that after excavation, its value will be even higher than the Cao Wang tomb in Anshang Village, Teng County. (9th)

Results of Huang Fu and Okamura's Negotiations; Content of Traffic Plan Secretly Guarded; Both Okamura and Yin Tong Express Optimism

----Dispatch

Beiping Correspondent: After Okamura Yasuji, the representative of the Japanese Kwantung Army, arrived in Beiping, he formally met with Huang Fu and He Yingqin at the Diplomatic Building the day before yesterday. The principles of various issues were negotiated and agreed upon. Detailed measures will be discussed and agreed upon as they are implemented. Huang and He went to the Fusang Hotel yesterday morning (8th) to visit Okamura in return. The conversation lasted about an hour. Okamura and others felt that their mission in Beiping had been completed and visited the Summer Palace today (9th) and are scheduled to go to Tianjin tomorrow (10th) to meet with Yu Xuezhong. After a brief discussion, they will return to Changchun by plane on the 12th. Yin Tong, the director of the Beining Railway Bureau, has drafted a concrete plan for the traffic issue on the Beining Railway. Xia Guangyu, a specialist sent by the Ministry of Railways to assist in the handling of the matter, submitted the plan to the Ministry of Railways for review. The content of the plan is strictly kept secret. However, it is reported that the only requirement is that, in addition to the vehicles of the Beining Railway, vehicles of other railways cannot enter Guan Nei. The Japanese side has formally recognized and returned the various passes of the Great Wall. Our side will send administrative personnel and security teams to receive them. The specific measures will be submitted by the Hebei Provincial Government to the Political Affairs Readjustment Committee for approval. The handover can be completed as soon as both sides agree. The procedure is not complicated and is expected to be realized in the shortest time possible. The Japanese army at each pass will only be able to withdraw completely at the end of the month. The establishment of customs is more complicated and requires detailed planning and measures from the Ministry of Finance. The postal issue is being studied to determine the method of using stamps. According to Yin Tong, the director of the Beining Railway Bureau, this morning, the opening of the Beining Railway has been decided by the bureau's administrative meeting. However, the content of the plan will be kept secret for the time being. The reception of the various passes of the Great Wall has been the result of Okamura's visit to Beiping. However, the opinions of the two sides on other matters have not yet been completely consistent. According to Okamura, his visit to Beiping was very satisfactory in discussing various issues with the two chairmen, Huang and He. The matters discussed were all agreed upon in principle, not concrete plans. The future of China and Japan will proceed according to these principles. Politically, there are still many difficulties, but economically, it is believed that cooperation can be gradually achieved. The return of the various passes of the Great Wall is of course no problem. The withdrawal of the small number of Japanese troops stationed within the war zone is also a matter of course. However, because the construction of labor camps outside Guanwai has not been completed, it will take some time. Opening to traffic and postal services are what we eagerly hope for. Although there has been no detailed discussion, we also hope to achieve this soon. From the talks of Yin Tong and Okamura, the content of the negotiations between the two sides in recent days can be glimpsed. (November 9)

The Xinjiang Incident: From Jin Shuren to Sheng Shicai, and the Relationship Between the Northeast Army and the New Situation

Dihua Correspondence: Since the founding of the Republic of China, internal wars have raged for years, and hardly any province has been spared. However, Xinjiang had remained relatively peaceful. Although there were occasional conflicts between the Hui and Han peoples, these were localized issues that were resolved through pacification. However, after Jin Shuren assumed power in Xinjiang, his mismanagement of military and political affairs, coupled with exorbitant taxes and levies, left the people with no means of survival. At the same time, he imposed a media blackout and implemented policies to keep the people ignorant. Political corruption was rampant, and bribery was commonplace. These factors led to the outbreak of the first Xinjiang Incident. The main players in this incident were Jin Shuren and Ma Zhongying. Jin was a Han Chinese, while Ma was a Hui. In addition to the struggle for power, there was also ethnic animosity between them, leading to mutual slaughter that claimed over ten thousand lives. When the fighting broke out, Jin realized that his troops (the current provincial army) were incapable of combat and retreated in defeat every time. He was eventually forced to flee, and command of the provincial army was handed over to his chief of staff, Sheng Shicai. At that time, Ma's army had advanced to a point very close to the provincial capital, vowing to kill all Han Chinese and establish a Northwest Hui Autonomous Alliance. He also sought to form a Hui nation by collaborating with Turkey. Ma was a young, radical leader of the Hui New Teaching sect. Even the assets of Ma Fuxiang's family were confiscated by him. However, despite his youth, Ma acted recklessly, relying solely on his courage and lacking modern knowledge and political ideas. He was essentially a chieftain from the tribal era.

After Jin fled, the remnants of his army were reorganized by Sheng Shicai, and the provincial government was taken over by Zhang Peiyuan, the commander stationed in Ili. At that time, Ma Zhongying was winning every battle and seemed poised for total victory. He sent plainclothes soldiers to operate in the suburbs of Dihua, resulting in the deaths of many Han Chinese. As a result, the city of Dihua was alarmed several times each night. Fortunately, over two thousand troops from the Northeast Anti-Japanese Army under Su Bingwen suddenly entered Xinjiang via Russia, and six thousand troops from the Jilin Self-Defense Army under Li Du also arrived from Russia. Su and Li's troops were not only well-disciplined but also highly capable in combat, greatly boosting the morale of the provincial army. The siege of Dihua was lifted, and the Han Chinese in the city welcomed them with food and drink. However, Su and Li's troops were reluctant to participate in the internal conflict. The generals sent letters to Ma Zhongying, urging him to stop the fighting and, at the very least, to strictly prohibit ethnic killings. Ma, emboldened by his victories, disregarded their pleas and continued his killing and looting. For the sake of the hundreds of thousands of Han Chinese and for their own self-preservation, Su and Li's troops resolutely assisted the provincial army (i.e., Sheng Shicai) in attacking Ma. Ma was decisively defeated, almost to the point of complete disintegration. In this battle, the Northeast Army suffered casualties including Brigade Commander Liu and Regiment Commanders Yu and Lu, illustrating the intensity of the fighting. After suffering a crushing defeat, Ma Zhongying retreated to Hami, Turpan, Shanshan, and other places, gathering his remaining troops, which numbered only four thousand, half of whom were old and weak. Sheng and Liu seized the opportunity to send a telegram to the entire nation, declaring themselves chairman and director, claiming to have been elected by the people. Sheng and Liu, having just started anew, had not yet consolidated their power, so they did not pursue Ma relentlessly. Instead, they seized the opportunity to call a truce, focusing on internal consolidation and seeking support from Soviet Russia. Ma also wished to use this time to recuperate and plan for a resurgence. Thus, the first incident came to an end, and the political power of Xinjiang fell into the hands of Sheng, Liu, and others, who continued to implement a policy of isolation. At this time, Sheng had essentially become the dictator of Xinjiang. When the central government ordered Huang Musong to enter Xinjiang to provide comfort and attempt to resolve the Xinjiang issue thoroughly, Sheng and Liu became greatly alarmed, fearing that their positions would be threatened. They decided to go all the way, placing Huang under house arrest as a condition for coercing the central government to issue military and political orders. At that time, mail and telegrams were censored, martial law was imposed, and the situation was extremely tense. Chen Zhong, Li Xiaotian, and others were unjustly shot dead. At this point, Sheng and his allies completely disregarded the central government.

Sheng Shicai currently has two infantry brigades, totaling 2,300 men, consisting of the original provincial army. They lack training and are prone to vices. In addition, there is a White Russian army brigade of 1,500 men, called the Naturalized Army, which is prone to drunkenness and disturbances and has very poor discipline. The Northeast Army captured over a thousand men in battle against Ma Zhongying's army, who were then formed into a guard regiment stationed at the governor's office. These thousand-plus men had been with Ma for a long time, so the people were generally fearful that they would be difficult to subdue. Recently, a mutiny occurred, further proving their unreliability. In short, Sheng's direct troops total over four thousand men, but only twenty to thirty percent are combat-ready. Sheng's ability to maintain his position is entirely due to the mutual constraints of the various factions. The Northeast Army, under the rallying cry of the Hui people that all Han Chinese must be killed, had no choice but to temporarily cooperate with Sheng Shicai for self-preservation. Zhang Peiyuan, in order to preserve his strength, sat back and watched the蚌鷸相爭 [idiom for two parties fighting and a third benefiting], waiting to reap the fisherman's reward. Thus, due to the balance of power, Xinjiang will fall into a state of perpetual turmoil. Unaware of this, people in society often mistake the Northeast Army for Sheng Shicai's own troops, but this is purely speculation and conjecture. The Northeast armies have their own history and system and will not be exploited by others.

As for Ma Zhongying, although he was defeated, he was not eliminated because he was a local native and a radical leader of the youth faction. Therefore, his latent power is greater than Sheng Shicai's. Thus, the current situation in Xinjiang has become a standoff between Sheng and Ma. Zhang Peiyuan only has three thousand troops and has not dared to attempt any of the previous struggles, believing that whoever wins between Sheng and Ma will not benefit him. As for Sheng's source of pride, it is his reliance on the support of the Northeast armies. Therefore, he is extremely ingratiating with the generals of the Northeast armies. The chief of staff of the directorate, the head of the military affairs department, the director of the arsenal, the officer of the military academy, the garrison commander of the provincial capital, and the commander of the guard regiment are all figures from the Northeast Army. On the surface, Sheng seems extremely humble and sincere, but he has ulterior motives. If the Northeast Army were to leave Sheng and remain neutral, the political situation in Xinjiang would change dramatically. This is because among the various factions in Xinjiang, the Northeast Army has the most men and the strongest fighting ability. The key to resolving the situation in Xinjiang in the future may lie here.

Situation of the Great Fire in Xuzhou - Location is the Emerging Commercial Center - Estimated Losses Exceed 500,000 Yuan

Xuzhou Correspondence: The Datong Street area of Xuzhou is a transportation hub connecting the city and the train station, and it is also an emerging commercial center. It is the most prosperous area in the city. Recently, due to social depression, the people's purchasing power has disappeared, and the shops on Datong Street have been holding competitive sales to attract customers. Lanterns and decorations are hung, and the night market is particularly lively. Recently, the Shanghai National Goods Touring Group arrived in Xuzhou, and Xuzhou also held a National Goods Promotion Week at the same time, setting up a market at the Garden Hotel to exhibit and sell goods. As a result, the shops on Datong Street became even more enthusiastic. Even the three or four shops that were usually closed for inventory and accounting temporarily opened to auction off goods. However, on the evening of the 8th, just as the electric lights were turned on, a fire suddenly broke out in the eastern section of the street. In an instant, the prosperous market was engulfed in flames, with people running away in panic, women crying, and children screaming. The scene was unbearable. The fire was extinguished at 9:00 p.m., after burning for four hours. Over eighty buildings were destroyed, and the losses are estimated to be at least 500,000 yuan. The details are as follows:

Cause of the Fire

At 5:00 p.m. on the 8th, shops on Datong Street, in order to promote sales, not only installed double the amount of electricity but also installed gasoline lamps for the convenience of the night market. The building in front of the Garden Hotel, built along the north side of the street, consisted of ten interconnected buildings, totaling ten upper floors and ten lower floors. The three westernmost buildings were the Tianzhang Silk Store, the four central buildings were the Xietongshun Silk Store, and the three easternmost buildings were the Yuanzhang Paper Store. A gasoline lamp on the upper floor of the Xietongshun Store exploded due to excessive pressure, spraying gasoline everywhere and scattering sparks. The Tianzhang and Xietongshun Stores had also installed large electric spotlights with high power, which also exploded as a result. Electricity and gasoline mixed and spread the fire. The goods piled up in these two stores were mainly wool, silk, and cotton textiles, while the Yuanzhang Store was entirely filled with paper, all of which were easily flammable. Therefore, within ten minutes of the fire starting, the ten upper and ten lower floors were completely engulfed in flames, and the fire was raging fiercely, making it impossible to approach. The crowd panicked. The police officer on duty frantically blew the whistle, and the fire brigade from the Public Security First Branch and Second Sub-branch was dispatched. At the same time, gongs were beaten to warn people, and various fire brigades rushed to put out the fire.

Spread of the Fire

After the building in front of the Garden Hotel was set ablaze, the temporary sheds set up behind the building for the National Goods Exhibition were quickly dismantled. Fortunately, the building was very tall, and the back walls were all made of brick and stone, so the fire did not spread. In front of the building, there was a row of workshops. The fire spread southward, igniting the Tonghegong Grocery Store across the street. The Jiufug Silk Store, which shared a wall with the Tonghegong Store on the east side, also caught fire. Flames flew across the street, and the fire brigades driving water hoses from the west could not pass through. They drove the hoses to the west of the fire and sprayed eastward. The fire brigades from Gulou Street and Wenting Street also set up water hoses to the west of the fire. At that time, the wind was blowing from the southwest to the northeast, so the fire did not spread westward but continued to spread eastward, setting fire to the front building of the National Goods Commercial Building on the north side of the street. The building was separated from the building in front of the Garden Hotel by only a small alley. The fire first spread to the Dacheng Cigarette Store on the west end, followed by the Zhonghua Shoe Store, the Juqinglong Grocery Store, the Dinghua Foreign Goods Store, the Meizu Clock and Watch Store, the Wild Rose Ice Room, the Yuanhetai Cigarette Store, and the main entrance of the Zhongjia Commercial Building, totaling eleven buildings. The fire became even more intense. Fortunately, the fire brigades from the Jinpu and Haizhou Railway Companies and the Dongguan Charity Fire Brigade arrived and set up hoses to the east of the fire to spray water. They also demolished the straw houses on the east side of the front building of the commercial building, preventing the fire from spreading further eastward. However, the building was also tall, and when the fire was raging, it spread to the opposite side of the street, setting fire to the Meihua Photo Studio and the Jiuzhang Military Uniform Store. The Nankai Fire Brigade arrived early from the New South Gate and set up hoses to the south of the fire to spray northward, preventing the fire from spreading southward. By about 8:00 p.m., the fire had begun to subside. At that time, black smoke billowed from the rubble, and the water hoses from the east and west were able to pass through the streets and engage in extinguishing the remaining embers.

Security and Maintenance

When the fire started, there were many visitors in the National Goods Exhibition Hall, and Datong Street was also crowded. People panicked and ran in all directions, causing great disorder. The Seventh Division Cadre Training Team, which was closest to the fire, was ordered by Education Director Zhou Tiren to deploy. Police officers from the Public Security Bureau rushed to the scene, and military and police posts were stationed on the streets and alleys. The visitors in the exhibition hall were blocked by the fire at the front gate and had to exit through the back door. At the height of the fire, Jinpu Garrison Commander Wang Jun, County Magistrate She Nianzi, Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Shicai, Seventh Division Political Training Director Long Ciyun, Second Recruitment Director Chen Xueshun, and various branch bureau chiefs and town chiefs all arrived at the scene to inspect and direct the maintenance of order. Therefore, the order was relatively good. However, the owners of neighboring shops who had not insured their goods moved their belongings to a more distant open space, piling them up like mountains. Some even watered quilts and covered them on the roofs to prevent the flames from spreading. The sound of crying and the sound of police whistles were heart-wrenching. Datong Street was covered in mud and water, with hardly a clean spot. After 9:00 p.m., the situation gradually calmed down, but the aftermath continued.

Stray Flames Cause Trouble

Between the front building of the Garden Hotel and the front building of the commercial building, there was a small alley with several straw houses. When the fire was raging, they were not set ablaze due to the distance. However, stray flames landed on the roofs, which was not noticed at the time. After the fire was extinguished and the distant water hoses had returned, the straw houses suddenly caught fire again, and whistles and gongs were sounded again. Fortunately, the fire brigade had not yet returned, and the water hoses that had returned halfway rushed back. In an instant, several straw houses were reduced to ashes. Fortunately, when the initial rescue was carried out, the roofs of the buildings had already been sprayed with a lot of water, preventing the fire from spreading. After 10:00 p.m., the fire was completely extinguished, and the embers were watered overnight. Datong Street was under martial law all night.

Loss Statistics

The losses from this fire, excluding the goods of the various shops, which are difficult to estimate accurately, include the following buildings destroyed: Six buildings on the north side of the street belonging to Tianzhang, eight buildings belonging to Xietongshun, and six buildings belonging to Yuanzhang. These were the buildings in front of the Garden Hotel, owned by Wu Jihong, with four kitchens attached behind the buildings. Two buildings belonging to Dacheng, four buildings belonging to Zhonghua, six buildings belonging to Juqinglong, six buildings belonging to Dinghua, and two buildings belonging to the main entrance of the commercial building. Two buildings belonging to the Wild Rose and Yuanhetai, and two buildings belonging to Meizu. These were the buildings in front of the commercial building, owned by the public, with two bungalows attached behind the buildings and a teahouse at the entrance of the small alley. Six buildings on the south side of the street belonging to Tonghegong, with three back rooms, two buildings belonging to Jiufu City, with one back room, owned by Wu Guangyuan. Three buildings belonging to Mei City, with one back room, three buildings belonging to Jiuzhang City, with three back rooms, owned by Tiancheng Company. In addition, there were three straw houses in the north alley. In total, eighty-three buildings of various sizes were burned down. If the construction costs and goods are included, the estimated losses are at least 500,000 yuan. However, the exact figures are still being thoroughly investigated. This is a true catastrophe. The Shanghai National Goods Touring Group did not suffer any losses. As for the people, one employee of the Xietongshun Store was slightly burned by the fire. Those who had insurance have already reported the incident. The authorities have already summoned the person in charge. As for the aftermath of the fire, the town chief and deputy superintendent of Datong have convened a joint meeting and will coordinate with the authorities to carry out all the necessary measures. (9th)

Nanchang Guyi Garden Opens for Chrysanthemum Viewing

Nanchang Guyi Garden is a famous scenic spot handed down from the Ming Dynasty. During the January 28 Incident, it was occupied by Japanese invaders for more than a month, and the scenery in the garden was almost completely destroyed. This summer, the local people, in order to preserve the historical site, initiated a fund-raising campaign for repairs by Chen Shaoyun, Wang Quanshi, Li Liangcai, and others. They received enthusiastic donations from local gentlemen and merchants in Shanghai, and the construction work has been completed. However, it is said that a part of the project has not yet been fully completed due to economic limitations, and the initiators are still working hard to proceed, expecting that the old appearance will be fully restored soon. Furthermore, the town formerly had a Chrysanthemum Society, led by Ge Zhirang, the owner of Ge Garden, which cultivated many fine species over the years. After the war, it was completely destroyed. This autumn, chrysanthemum art enthusiasts have worked hard to search and collect them, and they have found fine flowers from various places, no less than a thousand or several hundred species. They have been opened in time now, and the society is scheduled to hold a chrysanthemum exhibition at Guyi Garden for ten days starting on the 11th of this month, with beautiful colors and a dazzling array. It is now convenient to travel to the town, and trains and cars can reach it directly. Those who have the elegant taste of Yuanming are welcome to come and evaluate it.

Songjiang Zhu Zonghai Transferred to Jianngdu County Procurator

Zhu Zonghai, the procurator of the county court of this county, has been in office for more than a year. Mr. Zhu has recently been ordered to be transferred to Jiangdu County Court as procurator. He is currently preparing everything and is scheduled to go to Jiang to take office.

Lu Tuji Robbery Case Verdict

The family of Xue Guanrong, a farmer in Lutu Ji outside the South Gate, was robbed in July this autumn. At that time, the owner accused Shen Guichang, a detective of the Public Security Bureau, of colluding with the bandits and filed a lawsuit with the county court. After the evidence was summoned and interrogated, it has now been concluded, and the main text of the judgment was pronounced yesterday: In the case of Shen Guichang's robbery, Shen Guichang is not guilty.

Suzhou Jiangsu Provincial Public Servant Disciplinary Committee Established

The Jiangsu Provincial Public Servant Disciplinary Committee has been appointed with Lin Biao, President of the High Court, concurrently as Chairman, and Shen Yuan, Chief of the First Civil Chamber of the High Court, Lin Zhemin, Chief of the First Criminal Chamber, Hu Shancheng, Chief of the Second Criminal Chamber, Lu Wenlan, Chief of the Second Criminal Chamber, Zhang Bingci, Judge of the Second Criminal Chamber, Yao Yuanchu, Secretary of the Provincial Government, Wang Xizeng, Section Chief of the Civil Affairs Department, Huang Shaohong, Secretary of the Education Department, and Shen Baozhang, Secretary of the Construction Department, and other nine people as members. Yesterday (10th) at 10:30 a.m., an oath of office ceremony was held. The Judicial Yuan specially sent Yu Jingtang to Suzhou to supervise the oath. Luo Liangjian, the representative of the provincial government, and Duan Muzhen, the representative of the provincial party headquarters, both gave speeches. In the afternoon at 3 p.m., the association held its first committee meeting.

Wuxian Township Zonal Joint Defense

County Magistrate Zou, considering that the winter defense season has arrived, specially summoned the heads of the urban and rural areas yesterday (10th) to hold a joint defense meeting. After discussion, it was resolved that (1) Refer to the previous year's established case, from December 1 of this year to the end of March of the 23rd year, as the winter defense period, (1) The entire county is divided into six joint defense zones, (1) The urban and rural areas are the first joint defense zone, (2) The first, fourth, and twelfth districts are the first joint defense zone, (3) The second, third, fifth, sixteenth, eighteenth, and twentieth districts are the third joint defense zone, (4) The tenth, thirteenth, and fourteenth districts are the fourth joint defense zone, (5) The sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth, fifteenth, and areas are the fifth joint defense zone, (6) The fifth, seventeenth, and nineteenth districts are the sixth joint defense zone, (3) Elect the heads of the joint defense zones, (4) The heads of the joint defense zones shall convene relevant law and order authorities immediately, discuss defense affairs, and jointly plan for progress.

Wuxi Plans to Store Grain for Famine Relief

Gu Renfa, Director of the Civil Affairs Department of Jiangsu Province, in order to seriously focus on granary administration, specially stipulated regulations for organizing and storing grain, and issued instructions to the counties to comply with and implement them. After receiving the order, Yan Shenyu, the magistrate of the county, immediately transferred the order to the Food Administration Committee to be responsible for handling it. Yesterday (10th) at 2 p.m., the committee held a meeting in the county government conference room. The attendees included Committee Members Zhao Zixin (substituting for Gu Bingrong), Feng Junyan, Yan Shenyu, Cai Jian, Chen Zhanru, and Qian Sunqing, etc. The meeting was chaired by County Magistrate Yan, and the main case was discussed. In compliance with the order, plans are underway to store grain and prepare for famine relief. The county currently has more than 5,000 yuan in grain storage funds, which are legally used to purchase grain. In accordance with the established cases from previous years, districts, townships, and towns should also organize and store grain. All grain storage funds are not allowed to be used for other purposes. The meeting adjourned upon reaching this point.

Changzhou Murder Suspect Surrenders

Sun Shoufang, a young man from Lijia Bridge in Wu County, committed suicide in Zhenjiang earlier. In his suicide note, he mentioned that Liu Gengda, a well-known rogue from Lijia Bridge, brutally killed Li Yinhuan, a carpenter, in Zhenjiang, and that he should be avenged. After this matter was disclosed in the newspapers, the county court's procuratorate immediately sent personnel to investigate the village and found the burial place of Li Yinhuan's coffin. They immediately opened the coffin for examination and confirmed that the body had injuries. A warrant was then issued for the arrest of Liu Gengda, but he was never caught. On the 9th, Liu Gengda surrendered himself and submitted a statement to the procuratorate. Procurator Guan Junjie opened a court session for interrogation and ordered his detention.

Zhenjiang Garrison Command Established

The Zhenjiang Garrison Command was ordered to be organized during Gu Zhutong's term as chairman. However, due to the reorganization of the provincial government, it has not been established for a long time. After Xiang Zhizhuang, Director of the Security Office, took over, he was ordered by the provincial government to concurrently serve as commander and ordered to organize its establishment immediately. Now that all matters have been arranged, it was officially established yesterday. The headquarters is attached to the Security Office. All staff members, except for two or three additional clerks, are all transferred from the Security Office. At the same time, because there are not many affairs, the number of staff members transferred is also small, and they are not paid separately.

Nantong Renovation of Historical Sites

The Department of Education believes that the Japanese Tomb on Langshan Road in Nantong is a famous historical site in the southeast, which can promote the national spirit of resisting foreign aggression. It has specially ordered the county government to renovate it, and the department has also produced couplets for praise. A special ancestral hall has been built for Pu Ding, who died in the fight against the Japanese, and funds have been raised for the ancestral hall. A memorial service is held once a year. The pavilion of Wen Tianxiang crossing the sea in Shigang has also been renovated by the county government education bureau and the Shigang Folk Education Center, and funds for safekeeping have been raised.

Provincial Water Police Fourth District Headquarters to Move to Baoshan

The headquarters of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, originally located in Wusong, moved to Nantong after the January 28 Incident. Now, due to the inconvenience of office work, it has been approved by the Department of Civil Affairs to move to Baoshan and will be implemented next month.

Funing Notorious Bandit Chen Biren Arrested

Chen Biren, a notorious bandit in this county, robbed the China Bank in Jiaxing with bandit leader Zhu Hanqing and others last year. The National Government issued an order to arrest him. Unexpectedly, the bandit Chen and others fled and hid in their homes without being arrested. Yesterday (7th), Wei Yichen, the third platoon leader of the first company of the Gou Dun police battalion stationed in Gou Dun, arrested him in Sanzha Township and sent him to the police battalion headquarters for transfer to the county government for interrogation.

Hangzhou Parricide Verdict, Each Sentenced to Death

Chen Zhou, a woman from Shangsi Township, Hang County, is forty-two years old. Her husband died early, leaving only one daughter named Cai Feng, who is now thirteen years old. In April of last year, Xu Ayou was recruited as an adoptive son-in-law to live with his future wife in the Chen household until she matured for marriage. Although Chen Zhou was middle-aged, she still retained her charm and had an affair with her neighbor Ren Mingqian. Xu Ayou was deeply dissatisfied with this and often argued. Therefore, Chen and others harbored resentment and developed murderous intentions. On the night of September 30 of this year, they broke their adoptive son's scrotum and strangled him with a towel, making the corpse appear to have committed suicide by hanging himself, intending to shirk responsibility. The incident was discovered by the township office, and the Hangzhou District Court opened the coffin for inspection and confirmed the facts. Chen Zhou and Ren Mingqian were sent to the court, and witnesses were summoned. After clear investigation, they were deemed to have premeditated murder and prosecuted in accordance with Article 284, Clause 1, Item 1 of the Criminal Law. After repeated inquiries by Judge Jin Pingsen, Chen Zhou's daughter Cai Feng testified how she was murdered, with every detail painted vividly. Yesterday (10th) at 2:00 p.m., Chen Zhou and Ren Mingqian were each sentenced to death.

Mingguang Organizes a Seven-County Joint Defense Team

The seven counties of Chu, Lai, Quan, Jia, Tian, Han, and He under the jurisdiction of the Fifth Administrative Region are ordered to organize a joint defense. Each county will draw a platoon of security teams and organize a large defense team. The salaries are managed by the counties themselves. Guns and ammunition have been issued by the Third Provincial Bandit Suppression Headquarters.
