Tomorrow is the Anniversary of the Premier's Birthday - Unveiling Ceremony of the Bronze Statue to Be Held

Tomorrow (12th) is the anniversary of the birth of Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Kuomintang, and the unveiling ceremony of the Premier's bronze statue will be held at the same time. The commemorative measures drafted by the Municipal Party Headquarters are as follows: (1) Convene a memorial meeting for all sectors of Shanghai to commemorate the Premier's birthday; (2) The date is set for 9:00 a.m. on November 12; (3) The meeting place is the auditorium of the new Shanghai Municipal Government building in Jiangwan; (4) The presidium of the conference will consist of eight people, who will be representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Education Association, the Municipal Farmers' Association, the General Labor Union, the University Student Union, and the Two-Road Administration; (5) Starting from November 8, a five-day newspaper notice will be issued; (A) All sectors will take a day off on this day and celebrate by hanging flags. All party members in the city should participate in the meeting, and each group can send four or more representatives to participate; (B) Before the conference, all party members and representatives from all sectors will first hold the unveiling ceremony of the bronze statue of the Premier built by all sectors of Shanghai, and then hold a commemorative meeting; (6) Distribute 200,000 copies of small slogans; (7) The conference will have two recorders, two emcees, ten receptionists, and ten security guards, who will be designated by the secretary-general; (8) Issue a public announcement to the people commemorating the Premier's birthday; (9) Send a letter to the Municipal Security Office and the Public Security Bureau, requesting them to dispatch a number of troops and police to maintain order at the meeting place; (10) The conference sequence slogan will be distributed using silk-screen printing.

Notice of Participation

Regarding the notice, November 12 is the anniversary of the Premier's birthday. The association will convene a memorial meeting for all sectors of Shanghai at 10:00 a.m. on this day in the auditorium of the new Shanghai Municipal Government building in Jiangwan, and stipulates two measures: (1) All sectors will take a day off on this day and celebrate by hanging flags. All party members in the city should participate in the meeting, and all agencies, groups, and schools should send four or more representatives to participate before 9:30 a.m.; (2) Before the conference, all party members and representatives from all sectors will first hold the unveiling ceremony of the bronze statue of the Premier built by all sectors of Shanghai, and then hold a commemorative meeting. This notice is hereby issued, and it is hoped that all agencies, groups, schools, and party headquarters at all levels in the city will comply with and implement it. This is a special notice.

Conference Staff

Presidium: Tong Xingbai from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wu Tiecheng from the Mayor and Garrison Commander, Wang Xiaolai from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Zheng Hongnian from the Municipal Education Association, Yu Zhenhui from the Municipal Farmers' Association, Zhu Xuefan from the General Labor Union, Xue Guangqian from the University Student Union, and Huang Boqiao from the Two-Road Administration. Recorders: Tong Muge and Zhu Xuechun. Security Guards: Appointed by the Public Security Bureau, etc.

Ceremony Order

The order of events for the celebration of the Premier's birthday and the unveiling ceremony of the bronze statue memorial gathering and ceremony are as follows: (1) Everyone stands at attention; (2) Sing the Party anthem; (3) Unveiling (music plays); (4) Everyone gives the highest salute to the Party and national flag and the Premier's bronze statue; (5) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's last will; (6) Silence; (7) Report; (8) Speech; (9) Music plays; (10) Ceremony concludes.

Central Representative

The Municipal Party Headquarters believes that the celebration of the Premier's birthday and the unveiling ceremony of the bronze statue are attracting a large number of party members and people from all walks of life in the city, making it an unprecedentedly grand commemoration. Therefore, it has specifically telegraphed the Central Executive Committee, requesting them to send personnel to Shanghai for guidance. It is now heard from the Municipal Party Headquarters that they received a reply telegram from the Central Secretariat yesterday, stating that it was decided to invite Committee Member Wu Tiecheng to represent and provide guidance. The original telegram is as follows: "To the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee, we have received your telegram. The Central Committee has decided to invite Committee Member Wu Tiecheng to represent and provide guidance. Apart from sending a telegram, this is especially to inform you. Central Executive Committee Secretariat, Qingyin."

Municipal Government Instruction

Yesterday, the Municipal Government instructed its affiliated agencies to hold separate gatherings for commemoration. The original order stated, "For compliance: According to the document submitted by the Civil Affairs Office of this government, stating that the Central Executive Committee Secretariat's Secret Document No. 16941 opens with: 'The methods for commemorating the Premier's birthday this year have been stipulated by the Central Committee. The day will be a holiday, and the national flag will be flown throughout the country for celebration. Party, government, military, and police agencies, groups, and schools in various places should hold separate gatherings for commemoration. The senior party headquarters in each location may also consider holding representative conferences. However, during this time of national crisis, there is no need for excessive extravagance. In addition to reporting to the party headquarters of various provinces and cities for compliance, a corresponding letter is requested for verification and for passing on the order to those under their jurisdiction for compliance, etc.' Based on this, it should be followed. In addition to instructing the office to reply and circulate the instructions, all should comply, and subordinates should be instructed to comply as well. This order."

Citywide Business Closure

Since the Municipal Government instructed its affiliated agencies not to engage in extravagance, all agencies have decided to fly the flag on that day and hold commemorative gatherings at 10:00 AM. All schools, factories, groups, and customs, banks, etc., will be closed for the entire day. All fleets of the Navy Department will fire salutes every morning to mark the occasion.

Establishment Process

The planning and establishment of the Premier's bronze statue began seven years ago. With the enthusiastic participation of artists at home and abroad, many plaster models were obtained. After review by the review committee, the one sculpted by Mr. Jiang Xiaojian was selected, and sculpting began immediately. Later, due to changes in events, it was delayed for a long time. The statue was originally scheduled to be erected in front of the Shanghai North Railway Station to allow the people of the city to admire it, and a foundation stone laying ceremony had already been held. However, due to the outbreak of the January 28th Incident, the North Railway Station was severely damaged. The Special Committee and the Municipal Government consulted and decided to relocate it to the municipal center, behind the Municipal Government Building, as the location was originally intended for the construction of a Premier's Memorial Hall. After the agreement, the construction of the stone base was started. Its position is behind the Municipal Government Building, about 50 meters away, and also about the same distance from the Memorial Hall site. It has now been completed and is entirely paved with white stone. The bronze statue is being molded and cast in Mr. Jiang's Meifeng Gold Casting Factory.

Demeanor of the Bronze Statue

The bronze statue is about eight feet tall, connected to a bronze base, with patterns and designs carved around it. Including the base, it is about nine feet tall in total, weighing about one ton. It is dark green in color, coated with a chemical solution to reduce its luster and give it a bronze appearance, preventing it from peeling off. The statue is in Chinese dress, wearing a long robe and mandarin jacket, holding a felt hat in his right hand and a bamboo cane in his left. Although the demeanor is very peaceful, the face seems quite haggard. This statue was taken when the Premier went north to Tianjin in 1924. At that time, the Premier had already been running around for the revolution for decades, experiencing excessive hardship and gradually showing signs of aging. Looking at his demeanor, one can know the great spirit of the Premier's dedication to the revolution.

Relocation Yesterday

After the statue was completed, it was moved from the factory to the city center for erection at about 10:00 AM yesterday morning. In addition to Mr. Jiang's personal guidance, Li Dachao, Section Chief of the Municipal Government, also accompanied to supervise. The statue faces south, and the Memorial Hall will be built behind it.

Letter to the People of the Nation

The Preparatory Committee of Shanghai's various circles for the construction of the Premier's bronze statue, in order to arouse the enthusiasm of the people of the country for commemorating the Premier, specially published an article "How Should the People of the Nation Commemorate the Premier?" The article stated: "This committee was established in the summer of 1928. Earlier, the citizens of Shanghai, considering that the Premier Sun Yat-sen's achievements were brilliant, and his character was great, not only contributing to the Party and the country, benefiting the people, and providing for future generations, but also that his spiritual appeal and ideological leadership were sufficient to make the weak stand up, reverse decline, and change customs, seeking the hearts of the people in drowning and turning the tide from collapse, were advocated by the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Two-Roads Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc., to build a bronze statue of the Premier as a permanent memorial, and entrusted this committee to manage the matter. Although the review of the drawings slightly delayed the time in the past, what the citizens entrusted to this committee is now fortunate to have been successfully reported, and when the completion ceremony is held, it happens to coincide with the Premier's birthday. Seeing the brilliant bronze statue and performing the solemn ceremony, can this committee not feel ashamed of the citizens of Shanghai? However, although this committee is not ashamed of the citizens of Shanghai, this committee is actually ashamed of the Premier. Not only this committee, but also the citizens of Shanghai, and even compatriots throughout the country, should all feel ashamed of the Premier. The Premier was born on November 12, 1866, in a civilian family in Zhongshan, Guangdong, without any special reliance or superior environment. However, the Premier had the ambition to revive China since childhood. After graduating from the Hong Kong Medical School, he spared no effort to promote the revolution. After ten failures, he finally overthrew the autocracy and established the Republic of China. Subsequently, Yuan Shikai betrayed the country and claimed the title of emperor, Li Yuanhong destroyed the law and disrupted discipline, Zhang Xun restored the monarchy, and Cao Wu manipulated power, causing hardship for the people and shaking the foundation of the country. The Premier could not bear to sit idly by, so he again led the 'Anti-Yuan,' 'Protect the Constitution,' and 'Northern Expedition' campaigns, until the day he went north and passed away, he still earnestly said that 'saving China' was his goal. Unfortunately, reaching our generation, internal strife has been frequent and external troubles have come one after another. To this day, hundreds of counties in Jiangxi, Guangdong, Sichuan, Fujian, and other provinces are still reduced to bandit areas. The venue where we are standing today is the battlefield where the Japanese army galloped two years ago. And the four northeastern provinces that have been lost are even greater losses and unprecedented shame for our country. Embracing the broken rivers and mountains and comforting the haggard people, can we not feel ashamed of the Premier? If we encounter such a serious national crisis and still do not think of striving to be strong and avenging our shame, we are directly sinners of the Premier, and it is more than just feeling ashamed of the Premier. Therefore, our commemoration of the Premier should not be limited to erecting bronze statues and holding grand meetings. Bronze statues and grand meetings should be regarded as a reminder to ourselves rather than a commemoration of the Premier. If we have the sincerity to commemorate the Premier, we should carry on his legacy and take the Premier's ambition as our own ambition and the Premier's actions as our own actions. The invaded land in the Northeast has not been returned. How should we endure hardship and humiliation, boycott enemy goods, and strengthen national defense? The communist bandits in Jiangxi have not been eliminated. How should we donate wealth and grain to assist the soldiers and comfort the refugees? China is not the country of the government or a few people, 'Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the world.' How should we each fulfill our responsibility to save the country? How should we contribute our individual intelligence, physical strength, and wealth, and even our entire family and life, to assist the government and jointly relieve the national crisis? People have a common saying, 'The Second World War is about to break out in 1936 (i.e., 1936).' (Because most of the world's arms limitation treaties expire in 1935 and 1936.) At that time, China will inevitably become the battlefield for Japan, Russia, and other countries. If our country can actively prepare today, we may be able to turn around and become the Turkey after the First World War. Otherwise, if we are allowed to be slaughtered, we will inevitably become a semi-colony divided into four or five parts. The situation is urgent. There are only three years left before the world war. We should immediately catch up and first assist the central government in suppressing the bandits and comforting the refugees, and then strive for construction in a stable society to enrich the people's strength and enrich the country's strength. Time, time, will not come again. Let us not miss this last opportunity."

Parade by All Circles

Tomorrow, after the meeting in the city center for the unveiling of the Premier's bronze statue and the celebration of his birthday, people from all walks of life will parade in the Nanshi area. As of last night, more than 5,000 people from all walks of life have registered to participate. It is said that the citizens will pay close attention to the parade.

Kong Xiangxi Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Host a Tea Party for the Financial Community. Kong Talks About Funding for the Bandit Suppression Campaign and Denies the Issuance of New Salt Tax Treasury Bonds.

Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi flew to Jiangxi a few days ago in response to a telegram from Chairman Chiang to discuss the issue of suppressing the Red Army bandits. After staying in Jiangxi for a day, he took a plane back to Nanjing. Yesterday morning at 7:30, he arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing on an overnight train. At 5:00 PM, he held a grand tea party at his private residence on West Yanan Road to entertain the local banking community. Details are recorded as follows:

Xu and Zou Pay Respects

After arriving in Shanghai yesterday morning, Kong first received Xu Kan, Director of the National Treasury Department of the Ministry of Finance, and Zou Bingwen, Member of the Cotton Industry Control Committee of the Economic Commission, at his residence at around 9:00 AM. They talked for about an hour before departing. Kong then met with reporters from various newspapers. At 11:15 AM, he took a car to the Central Bank to work.

Bandit Suppression Funds

When Kong met with reporters from various newspapers yesterday, he first stated that his trip to Jiangxi to discuss issues such as funding for the bandit suppression campaign with Chairman Chiang had already yielded considerable solutions. The current situation of bandit suppression is very smooth. If we do not want to suffer from the poison of the Red Bandits, we should cooperate from top to bottom and actively assist the government in completely suppressing the Red Bandits.

Central Finance

The Central Finance has a monthly deficit of approximately 12 million yuan, totaling approximately 140 million yuan annually. The deficit for this month has been resolved. As for the overall financial solution, I have repeatedly stated that I am determined to act based on the four words: "increase revenue and reduce expenditure." China's annual expenditure is only 800 million yuan in Chinese currency. Considering New York City in the United States, its annual expenditure is 700 million US dollars, a difference of four times. Given China's large population, vast land, and abundant resources, there is no need to worry about resolving the small deficit.

Denies Salt Bonds

When reporters asked if the recent rumors that the Ministry of Finance planned to issue 120 million yuan of salt tax treasury bonds were true, Kong replied that this was absolutely not true. Kong also corroborated Navy Minister Chen Shaokuan's denial, saying that it was unfounded.

Tea Party Gathering

Around 5:00 PM, Kong held a tea party at his residence on West Yanan Road to entertain the local banking, financial, and other important figures. Those who attended included Bei Songsun of the Bank of China, Li Fusun of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Hu Mengjia of the Central Bank, Wu Yunzhai of the Jincheng Bank, Hu Bijang of the Zhongnan Bank, Xu Zhanliu and Xu Jiyin of the Zhejiang Xingye Bank, Qian Xinzhi of the Four Banks Joint Treasury, Wang Huaizhong of the Yexin Bank, Chuan Xiaoan of the Tongshang Bank, Fan Jimei of the Qiye Bank, Song Ziliang of the Guohuo Bank, Tong Wenrui of the Jiangzhe Bank, Ye Fuxiao of the Dalu Bank, Xu Fu of the Shanghai City Bank, Lin Kanghou of the Bankers' Association, Zou Xieqing and Yu Zuoting of the Money Trade Joint Treasury, Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Liu Hongsheng of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Yu Qiaqing of the Sanbei Company, as well as Du Yuesheng and Zhang Xiaolin, and over a hundred others. Kong, accompanied by Xu Jianping, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance, warmly welcomed them and served tea and refreshments. They all dispersed happily around 7:00 PM.

The Naming Ceremony of the Two-Road Aircraft Scheduled for the 18th at Hongqiao Airfield

European Armistice Day Today

Today is the 15th anniversary of the European Armistice Day. In this city, diplomatic and military officials of the former Entente countries, veterans, and representatives of the army, navy, business community, etc., will gather as usual at 8:30 AM in front of the Armistice Memorial Monument at the intersection of Edward Road to lay wreaths and commemorate the fallen soldiers. After 10:45 AM, the Union Church on Sima Road and the Catholic Church outside the New North Gate will hold special prayers. In the afternoon, the Cercle Sportif Français and the British Air Force Association will hold celebration banquets as usual. At 8:15 PM, there will be a similar grand banquet in the French Chamber of Commerce, which will be followed by dancing until late at night.

The British troops stationed in Shanghai will also hold an Armistice Day parade at the football field opposite the Jiaozhou Road barracks at 10:30 AM this morning. This year coincides with the rotation of the 1st Battalion of the Worcestershire Regiment and the 2nd Battalion of the Argyll and Sutherland Highlanders. Both armies will be inspected together, and the outgoing Commander Major General Fleming and the new Commander of the British Forces in the Shanghai area, Brigadier Teakle, will also conduct the inspection together. After Major General Fleming's final inspection today, he will return to England on the troop transport ship Neuralia next Tuesday.

Qi Zhanjiu of the Liaoning National Salvation Army Reports on the Anti-Japanese Struggle. Yesterday Afternoon, He Hosted the Press at the Atlantic Restaurant. He Led His Troops of More Than 50,000 Men in a Bitter Two-Year Battle.

Qi Zhanjiu, Commander-in-Chief of the Liaoning National Salvation Army, along with Sun Yunwu, Chief of Staff, and Dou E, a representative of the army, returned from the front lines of Liaoning and arrived in Shanghai on the 7th. Yesterday afternoon at 6:00 PM, he hosted the press at the Atlantic Restaurant to report on the experience of raising the banner of righteousness and leading his iron-blooded warriors in a bloody battle against the Japanese army since the September 18th Incident. The full text of the report is recorded as follows:

Since the September 18th Incident, Zhanjiu and others, as active-duty soldiers, have fulfilled their natural duty to defend the border, united the Liaoning Provincial Border Defense Army, the people's militia of various counties in southern and western Liaoning, and patriotic volunteers, and organized the Liaoning National Salvation Army, totaling more than 50,000 people, to carry out the anti-Japanese work, fighting bitterly for two years. Initially, six divisions were formed, stationed in the mountains and forests of various counties in western Liaoning and southern Liaoning, acting according to circumstances.

Destroying Railways

When the Japanese invaders were probing into Jilin and Heilongjiang and attacking Jinzhou, Zhanjiu ordered the Third, Fourth, and Fifth Divisions to specialize in destroying the Yingkou-Jinzhou Railway and assist the provincial army in holding Dahushan and preventing enemy ships from transporting goods along the Liao River. The First, Second, and Sixth Divisions were tasked with destroying the South Manchurian Railway, from Shenyang to Haicheng, intercepting supplies from Dalian, disrupting the Japanese base in South Manchuria, and hindering the implementation of control near Fushun and the completion of highways in various counties. After Jinzhou fell on January 3 of last year, Zhanjiu ordered the divisions to continue working according to the original plan, and at the same time, contacted Zhang Haitian in Panxi West (i.e., Old Beifeng), Lu Shijie near Yingkou, Deng Tiemei on the Anfeng Line, and other units to engage in recovering the lost counties in western and southern Liaoning as a base for long-term resistance. Fortunately, the soldiers were brave, and within a few months, they successively occupied Panshan, Tai'an, Liaozhong, Liaoyang, Haicheng, Fengcheng, Niuzhuang, and other counties. This was the most prosperous period since the anti-Japanese war.

Painfully Retreating

This spring, after the loss of Rehe, the Japanese invaders invaded North China, and the armies guarding the Great Wall rose up to resist. Taking advantage of this opportunity, Zhanjiu and others contacted friendly forces and attacked Yingkou, intending to cut off the enemy's transportation throat. In the end, they failed due to the enemy's strong defenses and fierce artillery fire. After entering summer, the green gauze tent rose, and the Japanese guards along the South Manchurian, Yingkou-Jinzhou, and Fengtian lines were all killed or scattered by Zhanjiu's troops. From Shenyang in the north to Yingkou in the south, Panshan in the west, and Fengcheng in the southeast, there were no traces of the Japanese army within the borders of the counties. After the Mid-Autumn Festival, the people successively harvested their crops. Except for the mountainous areas, which could be used for concealment and defense, there were no long objects in the wilderness, and enemy reconnaissance was extremely easy, making it inconvenient to advance. In addition, the Tanggu Ceasefire Agreement was signed, and the Japanese puppet army deployed an additional four divisions of reinforcements. It could be predicted that a lonely army that had been fighting hard for more than two years, without any supplies, could not withstand the newly built enemy. Therefore, they temporarily abandoned the areas won through bloody battles and retreated to the mountains and forests to await an opportunity.

Latent Strength

Zhang Haitian's troops (now led by Zhang Zi (Little Beifeng) with more than 4,000 people are currently lurking in the mountains near □□ County. Lu Shijie's troops with more than 3,000 people are currently lurking along the coast of □□. Deng Tiemei's troops with more than 10,000 people are currently defending the mountains between □□□ and □□. The entire army of the exhausted army is now retreating to the Liaodong □□ area. After the exhausted army retreated, the troops were reorganized, the old and weak were eliminated, and the elite were selected to form four brigades, totaling more than 16,000 people, with complete firearms and more than 8,000 war horses. We also recruited patriotic volunteers and young soldiers from all sides for strict training, hoping to become an elite force.

The Reality of the Puppet State

Under the control of the Japanese invaders, the puppet state, although nominally occupying four provinces, can only effectively implement its policies in the cities and towns along the railway line. The remote counties and villages far from the railway are beyond the reach of the puppet state's power. The first step in the puppet state's political facilities is to force people to plant opium, promote open gambling, and collect heavy taxes to prolong their lives. In all the cities and towns where the Japanese and puppet forces can reach, opium dens and gambling houses are lined up, and the owners of the opium dens and gambling houses are all run by the Japanese. It is dark and unbearable to speak of. The reason why the Japanese are doing their best to force people to indulge in opium and gambling is purely to anesthetize the people of the Northeast, wear away their rationality, and block their self-improvement hearts. The Japanese invaders also installed telephones in the towns under their jurisdiction and used local tyrants and gentry to serve as scouts to prevent righteous armies from detecting public sentiment. The contemptible means are infuriating. Wherever our army arrives, we first ban opium and gambling, destroy the transportation network of the exhausted people, and start anew with the people. This is enough to show that the hearts of the people in the Northeast are not dead, and it is also the main reason why our army can support for two years. The puppet state now has 150,000 national defense troops. Those in Liaoning and Ning are the units of Yu Zhishan and Wang Dianzhong, those in Jilin are the units of Yu Xianzhou and Ji Xing, those in Heilongjiang are the units of Zhang Wen□ and Sun □cang, and those in Rehe are the units of Zhang Haipeng. Each army is monitored and commanded by the Japanese. All soldiers usually do not fire a single bullet, and are only issued by name when they are about to go into battle, because the Japanese invaders have never trusted the puppet army, fearing that the puppet army will revolt, and the defense is meticulous. However, under these circumstances, the puppet army's heart of revolt has not been completely eliminated. For example, recently, Zhang Xudong, the company commander of the machine gun company of Yu Zhishan, led the entire company to revolt and joined the Line Army, which is one example.

Future Aspirations

Zhan Yuan and others feel that the national atmosphere is very depressed after entering the customs. The previous patriotic upsurge has suddenly subsided. It must be known that the four northeastern provinces are the lifeline of the Republic of China, and how can we bear to see them being slaughtered and not feel pain in our hearts? There is no greater mourning than a dead heart, blood and tears are exhausted, what more can be said? Looking at the small and weak Turkey, there is still a Kemal who restored the country. The vast China does not have a Napoleon who will revive the country. Zhanjiu and others are confident that the government officials are experienced and deliberate in their plans, and work diligently day and night, and the plan to recover the lost land must have been carefully planned long ago. Moreover, the people of the Northeast and the soldiers of the puppet army are unwilling to be oppressed and hope that the government will send troops to recover the lost land, like a great drought hoping for a blessing. It is especially hoped that the people of the whole country will revitalize the spirit of self-improvement, eradicate the concept of temporary peace, unite from top to bottom, and never yield until death, as a backing for diplomacy and as a preparation for counterattack. Furthermore, we should use our remaining strength to assist the righteous army outside the customs, so that patriotic volunteers are not eliminated by the enemy. Once the Japanese-Russian war breaks out, our army can leave the Great Wall and defeat the strong enemy. The righteous army outside the customs can also disrupt the enemy's rear, supporting each other, destroying the Japanese-puppet transportation. The puppet army will be able to respond to the news, and the lost land will be recovered. This is just a matter of advice. I only hope that the people of the country will devote their loyalty and wisdom, destroy their families to relieve the nation's difficulties, and the survival of the country and the nation is at stake. Zhanjiu and others are committed to the country and determined to resist Japan. We will temporarily continue to work hard to repay the people of the country.

Harbor Quarantine Station's Fourth Anniversary Banquet Last Night: Wu Lien-teh Details Quarantine Work

The Harbor Quarantine Station held its fourth-anniversary banquet at the East Asia Restaurant last night at 7 p.m. Over a hundred guests attended, including Liu Ruiheng, Director of the National Health Administration; Liu Hongsheng, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company; Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce; Yuan Lidun; Li Ting'an; Dong Xian Guang; and representatives from various foreign consulates. They were warmly received by Dr. Wu Lien-teh, Director of the station, and others. During the banquet, Director Liu Ruiheng of the Health Administration gave a speech, followed by Dr. Wu Lien-teh, who detailed the station's work and current situation. Finally, Dr. Parker and Mr. Brown delivered speeches. The guests and hosts parted joyfully around 10 p.m. The following is a record of Dr. Wu Lien-teh's speech:

It is a great honor to have you esteemed guests grace us with your presence today. Despite your busy schedules, you have taken the time to attend, which encourages us in the progress of our station. All our work relies on the assistance and guidance of various parties; otherwise, we would not be able to make any progress. Regarding the representatives of the League of Nations present tonight, I would like to express my gratitude on behalf of our station. Without the assistance of the Health Section of the League of Nations over the past four years, our station would not have achieved such results. In particular, Dr. Rajchman, the Director of the Health Section of the League of Nations, has contributed greatly. I not only thank him but also take this opportunity to congratulate him on his new appointment as the League of Nations' representative for technical cooperation and advisor to the National Economic Council. Not only will our country benefit from this, but the world's economic future will also shine brightly. The cooperation between the League of Nations Health Section and our station has been further enhanced through the liaison of the Eastern Bureau of the Health Section in Singapore. Tonight, Dr. Parker, the Director of the Bureau, is also present. I would like to express my gratitude to him. Since taking office, he has been greatly concerned about the progress of our station and has provided full assistance. Before reporting on our work, I still have a point to clarify: Sir Frederick Maze, Inspector General of Customs, various foreign consuls, the Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, the French Municipal Council Health Department, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the Lister Institute, and leaders of the shipping industry have all provided our station with utmost convenience and cooperation. Our station's ability to fulfill its duties depends on the enthusiastic assistance of various public and private organizations in this city. As the scope of our duties expands daily, this mutual assistance will continue to advance without end. Now, I will briefly describe the general situation of our work this year.

Rat and Flea Research: I have heard people say that harbor quarantine is not an important task, and some even claim that its only effect is to delay the reunion of long-separated couples. There is no need to argue with such misunderstandings. Now, please allow me to discuss one of the most important parts of our station's work, which is the inspection of rats and rat fleas in Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, Xiamen, and Guangzhou. The purpose of this research is twofold: first, we want to obtain a reliable basis for the types of rats and their parasites in the above-mentioned ports; second, based on this basis, we can seek the interrelationship of plague transmission, as this disease often has the potential to invade with cargo ships. At the end of the 19th century, it invaded our country from India, then entered Taiwan and Japan. Therefore, Shantou, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Hong Kong, Guangzhou, and other ports were all invaded, except for Shanghai and the Yangtze River basin. However, on October 30, 1908, a Chinese person in Hankou was found to have contracted plague. This person originally resided in Shanghai. Since then, Shanghai has occasionally experienced rat plagues and mild epidemics. Therefore, under the guidance of the Chief Medical Officer of our station, we are engaged in this rat and flea research. The results obtained in the future are quite noteworthy. Over the past two years, a total of 2,000 rats have been inspected, all captured along the coast. Senopyila Cheoprs rat fleas are the best vectors for transmitting plague. According to the inspection, these plague fleas are only more numerous in late summer and autumn, with an index below one. It is not yet known whether the numbers obtained in the port area are consistent with those obtained in the urban area. In the near future, we plan to expand the scope of inspection to residential and commercial areas. The results obtained from inspections in other ports are significantly different compared to this city. Plague fleas breed throughout the year. Almost all the rat fleas obtained in Guangzhou and Xiamen are plague fleas. I must thank the owners of wharves and warehouses for allowing us to continue catching rats inside.

Cholera Situation

In the past few years, our station has become a general liaison organization because it is in charge of the Shanghai Temporary Cholera Prevention Office. Regarding cholera, we are now striving to carry out various chemical experiments and research in order to eradicate this evil epidemic completely. Last year, more than 4,000 people in this city suffered from cholera, but this year, there has been not a single case. Nationwide, there were approximately 100,000 patients last year, but only six this summer. At next year's anniversary banquet, I may be able to report on the results of our research. Although no true cholera cases have been found in this city this summer, there are still cases of dysentery, typhoid fever, and watery diarrhea. According to reports from the Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, there have been 28 cases of false cholera and watery diarrhea, and 485 cases of gastroenteritis.

Ship Inspection

The work of this section is quite difficult due to misunderstandings from the outside. When various ships enter from epidemic ports, quarantine work is very important, and it is inevitable that this will cause disturbance. I would like to tell the shipping industry that our station is not adopting any new policies, but only knows how to comply with international regulations, actively prevent the spread of quarantinable diseases, and strive to avoid hindering the shipping industry. Due to the global recession, the number of ships entering this city and other ports has decreased sharply. Fewer ships have been inspected than last year, but the total tonnage is almost the same. This year, no smallpox or cholera epidemics have been found in the coastal ports along the river, so the number of inspections has also decreased accordingly. In the ten months of 1933, a total of 1,954 ships were inspected, with a total tonnage of 12,552,579. During the same period last year, there were 1,969 ships, with a total tonnage of 12,576,414. By nationality, this year's inspections include 602 British ships, accounting for 32.5% (total tonnage 4,579,174); 628 Japanese ships, accounting for 32.9% (total tonnage 3,074,120); and 208 American ships, accounting for 11.3% (total tonnage 2,229,000). There were 111 Norwegian ships, 87 German ships, 50 Danish ships, 34 French ships, 35 Chinese ships, 32 Dutch ships, 20 Italian ships, 12 Swedish ships, 6 Panamanian ships, 4 Chilean ships, 5 Greek ships, and 13 Soviet ships. The inspectors at our station have very harmonious relationships with the crew members of various ships, which I am very fortunate for.

Ship Fumigation

In order to comply with the International Health Convention promulgated in 1926, the fumigation department of our station has fumigated a large number of ships this year, including ocean liners, cargo ships, river and sea vessels, and barges. We have also made every effort to guide rat prevention methods. The number of fumigated ships is listed below:

January to October 1933: A total of 646 ships were fumigated, with a hold tonnage of 1,387,134.

January to October 1934: A total of 720 ships were fumigated, with a hold tonnage of 1,584,123.

January to October 1933: 105 ocean liners were fumigated.

January to October 1934: 123 ocean liners were fumigated.

January to October 1933: 541 river and sea vessels were fumigated.

January to October 1934: 597 river and sea vessels were fumigated.

January to October 1933: 107 cargo ships were fumigated with carbon dioxide.

January to October 1934: 130 cargo ships were fumigated with carbon dioxide.

January to October 1933: 537 empty ships were fumigated with sulfur.

January to October 1934: 589 empty ships were fumigated with sulfur.

January to October 1933: 2 ships were fumigated with hydrocyanic acid.

January to October 1934: 1 ship was fumigated with hydrocyanic acid.

January to October 1933: 7 Rat Exemption Certificates were issued.

January to October 1934: 10 Rat Exemption Certificates were issued.

January to October 1933: 1,981 rats were fumigated to death.

January to October 1934: 2,276 rats were fumigated to death. No plague germs were found in any of them.

Medical Work: Due to the preparation for cholera and the occurrence of quarantinable diseases, our team's medical work, in addition to vaccinations and injections, is not very tense. After the Sino-Japanese War last year, the Wusong Clinic has been reopened. In the ten months of this year, a total of 1,220 people have been vaccinated by our station, including 426 travelers to Java and 279 French sailors going to Saigon. A total of 337 people from ship companies, dock workers, and sailors have been vaccinated against cholera.

Overview of Branch Offices: At the last anniversary banquet, I gave a brief report on the work of the quarantine branch offices in various ports. Now, please allow me to briefly describe the achievements of the Xiamen branch office, as it is the most important branch office besides the Shanghai branch office. Before January 1931, the quarantine work of the branch office was undertaken by private doctors hired by the Customs, and fees were charged for vaccinating outbound immigrants and inspecting inbound ships. However, there was no hospital to accommodate patients. After we took over, the local authorities allocated a large piece of coastal public land, and we immediately started building an isolation hospital. In the winter of that year, the hospital was completed. At the same time, there was a major smallpox epidemic, and many patients were admitted. Last year, when cholera was prevalent nationwide, the hospital's work was quite tense. A total of 20,000 people were vaccinated. Among the 197 patients treated, 49 died. There was an existing immigrant office in the port, but the location was poor, so it was decided to rebuild a new office and a first-class ward. The new building was funded by the vaccination and inspection fees previously collected. On September 30 of this year, I personally went to the Eastbound opening ceremony. Local officials, foreign consuls, and people from the shipping industry attended. The British Consul also handed over a check for over 8,000 yuan, which was the remaining donation from the old immigrant office. I must express my gratitude to the enthusiastic assistance of various Chinese and foreign parties. The work of the branch offices in North China has been somewhat difficult due to the situation, but they are still working hard according to the original plan. The fumigation work in Hankou has made good progress, and it has now been decided to slightly expand the scope of the branch office's work in that port. From the above brief report, it can be seen that I attach great importance to research and investigation. Medicine, like other sciences, is not static and unchanging. Regarding the prevention of epidemics from entering various ports, we pay considerable attention to various preventive issues related to our country and other countries. We sincerely hope that in a few years, we will be able to make further progress in solving the problem of epidemic outbreaks.

Dispute Over Transportation of Domestic Goods to Fujian: Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Mediates Yesterday

Both Parties Express Satisfaction and Acceptance

The dispute between the Shanghai China National Products Sales Cooperation Association and the Fujian gang Sanshan Guildhall over the transportation of goods to Fujian has been reported in the newspapers. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce believes that the occurrence of this incident is very unfortunate for the future of domestic goods and should be resolved peacefully as soon as possible. Therefore, at 2 p.m. yesterday, it invited representatives from both parties, as well as representatives from the shipping and customs brokerage trade associations, to a meeting to discuss a solution. Attendees included Wang Xiaolai and Lu Wenshao, representatives from the General Chamber of Commerce; Yao Zilun, Huang Renwu, Chen Runnan, and Huang Jiaxiang, representatives from the Sanshan Guildhall; Du Chongyuan, Lu Qiant, and Gui Yanfang, representatives from the China National Products Sales Cooperation Association; Yu Shunmao and Chen Xiangxiong, representatives from the Shipping Association; Shi Zhikun, representative from the Customs Brokerage Association; and Chen Jinchen, Zhou Zongren, and Lei Nai'er, representatives from the Jiangxi and Northern Fujian Business Associations in Shanghai, totaling 15 people. Wang Xiaolai, as chairman, first reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that the power of domestic goods is only in its infancy, and in any case, one party cannot dominate the overall situation. Even in terms of business relations, both parties can discuss mutually beneficial methods. It is essential to avoid harming each other and allowing foreign goods to extend their power. Chinese shipping companies should treat domestic products equally and support each other. Relationships based on personal feelings should not be used to favor one side over another. Now, more merchants who run domestic goods, the country will have less profit outflow, we are of the same root, please do not push too hard. Subsequently, representatives from all parties expressed their opinions one after another. Then, the representative of the Sanshan Guildhall proposed three requirements to resolve the case: (1) In the future, if the Sanshan Guildhall finds that the goods transported to Fujian are not domestic products, the National Products Sales Association can notify the Guildhall to handle the matter; (2) The National Products Sales Association shall not engage in contracting activities with manufacturers in Shanghai; (3) The National Products Sales Association shall only fulfill its role of introduction and shall not set up public sales offices in Fujian again. After the chairman's efforts to mediate, the association's representatives denied the second and third requests on the spot, and they were no longer a problem. It was decided that in order to avoid conflicts in business operations in the future, the association will give priority to the Sanshan Guildhall's customers for goods transported to Fujian, and the Sanshan Guildhall will no longer interfere with the association's domestic goods transported to Fujian. If the people of Fujian later establish a domestic goods company on their own, it will not involve the association. After the chairman persuaded both parties with this plan, they both expressed satisfaction and acceptance. The meeting adjourned at 4:30 p.m.

Zheng Quanzhong from Fujian Urges the Sanshan Guildhall to Cooperate with the National Products Introduction Office

Zheng Quan telegraphed, saying, "Shanghai Sanshan Guildhall, Fujian business firms, Fuzhou General Chamber of Commerce, and all business firms are hereby notified that reports indicate that the Shanghai Fujian gang, due to the National Products Introduction Office's efforts to transport domestic goods to Fujian for sale at low prices, which they consider to be detrimental to their business, have agreed with various shipping companies to refuse to transport domestic goods. This is deeply shocking. Promoting domestic goods is the only way for the people to save the country. Is Fujian going to reject domestic goods and be a dumping ground for foreign and enemy goods? If the country is gone, what business will there be? By only caring about current business and ignoring the disaster of national subjugation in the future, what kind of people will the country see us Fujianese merchants as? The patriotism of the Fujianese people is especially strong, as recorded in history. Please do not let the legacy of Zheng Chenggong and the martyrs of Huanghuagang be ruined by us. Please change your ways and work with the National Products Introduction Office to promote domestic goods. Sell off the accumulated foreign goods. In the future, unless there are no domestic goods to replace them, we must only sell domestic goods. Welcome domestic goods, everyone feels the same. Selling domestic goods exclusively will surely receive enthusiastic support from the people, and business will definitely develop abnormally. Conversely, if the people hate you, unexpected losses will be unpredictable. How can those who are cursed by everyone survive? The telegraphed tears cry, not knowing the turning clouds, Zheng Quan, trapped."

Relief Appeal from the Fujian Disaster Area Relief Association – Reception for the Press Yesterday

The Fujian Disaster Area Relief Association yesterday hosted a reception for newspaper reporters, with over twenty reporters from various newspaper offices attending. The chairman, Gan Ji Gong, presided over the event. During the gathering, the chief of general affairs, Xie Yinpo, stood up and delivered a report, stating approximately: “Today, we members of the association are honored to have all the gentlemen from the press present to provide guidance, for which we are extremely grateful. The rampant spread of the Red disaster in Fujian originated five years ago. At that time, it was confined to a part of western Fujian, the den of the Red bandits Zhu De and Mao Zedong. Their strength was originally extremely fragile, but due to the local authorities’ lack of attention, it was allowed to spread. Gradually, their fierce flames grew and engulfed western Fujian. Once they had fully developed their power, they proceeded to disturb Jiangxi, leading to the nationwide catastrophe we face today. It is extremely heartbreaking to speak of this. Last year, the Red bandits attacked and captured Zhangzhou, and the central government dispatched the 19th Route Army to aid Fujian. However, the bandits retreated before the army arrived, maintaining a small-scale balance of power for nearly a year. Recently, the highest military authorities encircled and suppressed the bandits, while simultaneously blockading food supplies in the bandit-controlled areas. Unable to succeed, the bandit leaders, including Peng Dehuai, launched a full-scale invasion of Fujian. Their advance was quite sharp. In the battles of Liancheng and Qingliu, the garrison troops were ultimately defeated due to a significant disparity in numbers. The bandit army then seized the opportunity to attack Yanping and probe Youxi, threatening to approach the Fujian capital. Fortunately, the 56th Division heroically defended Jiang Le and Shunchang with their isolated forces. They held out for fifty days, running out of ammunition and food. The defense of Shunchang by Tang Tu Chang, in particular, deserves our commendation. It is said that the number of bandits involved in this rebellion exceeded ten thousand, while Tang's troops were outnumbered ten to one. Upon the arrival of the bandits, they immediately closed the city and defended it to the death. When the rice in the city ran out, they replaced it with flour. When the flour ran out, they replaced it

Page 12

with dried bamboo shoots. The military and civilians shared these equally, uniting as one. Although the Shun army bombarded the city day and night with heavy artillery, the officers and soldiers across the country swore to fight to the death and remained unmoved. The city ultimately survived. If all our anti-bandit generals could be like Commander Tang, the Red bandits would not be difficult to subdue. As for the Shaxian and Yong’an areas, they were jointly defended by Mao Weisou's and Lu Xingbang's troops. The bandits launched repeated attacks and suffered heavy losses. The bandits in Yanping, realizing that they could not succeed in capturing Shaxian and Yong’an, also withdrew. Simultaneously, the central government's support troops, including those of Guan Tao and Zhou Hunyuan, had already arrived in Fujian, lifting the siege of various counties in northern Fujian. Tracing back, our province has suffered the ravages of the Red bandits for five years. The area affected by the current disaster extends throughout western and northern Fujian. The displacement and migration of disaster victims in various counties, those who have no homes to return to, number over a million. The destruction of houses and fields, and the massacre of men, women, old, and young, are even more countless. The severity of the disaster and the extent of the affected area are no less than those in Jiangxi. Considering the devastation of our homeland and the disaster victims awaiting relief, our fellow countrymen should urgently gather various overseas organizations to establish a disaster relief organization. Just as we were discussing this, Mr. Sa Zhenbing, formerly from Gongsa Township, came to Shanghai from Fujian to raise relief funds. Various hometown associations held a meeting to welcome him. Considering that Mr. Sa has been in charge of Fujian relief efforts for many years and is highly trusted by all sectors of society, it was unanimously decided to initiate the establishment of the Fujian Disaster Area Relief Association, with Lu Gong as the chairman and Chen Shao嬀 and Xu Yungong as the vice-chairmen. A custody committee was also established, with the Zhongnan Bank, Xiamen Bank, Overseas Chinese Bank, Zhongxing Bank, and various guild halls responsible for managing the relief funds. Initially, a large sum of money was raised by the various guild halls to provide emergency relief. Meanwhile, solicitation teams were organized, with groups, businesses, and individuals taking responsibility for fundraising, aiming for collective effort and maximizing contributions. Since the establishment of our association, letters and telegrams reporting disasters have flooded in like snowflakes. To comprehensively plan and understand the actual situation in the disaster area, in addition to issuing survey forms to the Fujian Provincial Government, the Pacification Commissioner’s Office in Fujian, various county governments, county party headquarters, legal entities, and local impartial individuals for them to fill out and return at any time, we are also selecting and dispatching special envoys to the disaster area to conduct investigations as the basis for relief distribution. However, this matter is of great importance, and it is absolutely beyond our capabilities to shoulder this heavy responsibility alone. We hope that people from all walks of life across the country will rise up and provide strong support for our association. Furthermore, as mentioned above, the Fujian bandit disaster affects the entire country. We also believe that the vitality of the region is the vitality of the country. In the future, the reconstruction of the disaster area should also be the responsibility of the government. We hope that the national relief agencies will pay close attention to and assist the disaster situation in Fujian. At the same time, we hope that the press will disclose our association's subsequent measures and the detailed information about the disaster area obtained from various sources in a timely manner, so as to attract the attention of the people of the country and jointly seek a thorough elimination of the communists and disaster relief. This is not only the fortune of Fujian but also the fortune of the entire country.” Finally, Chen Ni and Shangguan Shufang delivered speeches successively. The reception adjourned at four o'clock.

Resolution of Fishery Construction Disputes

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce Sends Personnel to Mediate and Advise

The collection of fishery construction fees in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has sparked opposition from fish merchants, dragging on for months without resolution. Yesterday, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce specially dispatched Counselor Yu and Secretary Xu, along with the original mediators Yu Qiaqing, Du Yuesheng, and Yu Zuoting, to send letters inviting leaders of the frozen seafood industry, including Liu Yuehua, Zhang Zhenfang, Chen Jiushou, Shen Xianlu, Wang Zuquan, Chen Linfu, Zheng Yunsheng, and Huang Zhensheng, to the Guangdong Chelu Shipping Club for a final mediation. All parties were candid and open. After several hours of consultation, a settlement was reached. The five settlement measures are excerpted below: (1) The fishery construction fee will be collected on behalf of the frozen seafood industry company through persuasion and guidance. (2) The construction fee will not be levied in areas where domestic salted fish, dried seafood, and shellfish are sold, and there will be no detention of goods. (3) The construction fee will be levied on barrel-headed fresh fish at the time of the first entry into the trade. Shanghai will not collect it again. If it is not collected, the Shanghai trade will collect it on behalf. If there are obstacles, the collection office will be notified to handle it. (4) The fishery construction fee will be based on the principle of one percent of the value. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce will provide appropriate guarantees. If there are any changes, the opinion of the guild must be sought first. (5) The fishery construction fees collected on behalf of the Frozen Seafood Industry Guild will be collected and remitted by the guild. If the collection office deems it necessary to audit, it may send personnel to jointly audit the trade association with the guild representatives. Counselor Yu of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce also verbally acknowledged that frozen seafood businesses could appoint representatives to participate in the management of the fishery construction fee.

Han Yougang Requests Thorough Investigation of Corruption in the Fisheries Bureau

Han Yougang, the former director of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Regional Fisheries Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, recently heard that Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, in a proposal to the Executive Yuan on the collection of fishery construction fees, stated that former directors had engaged in corruption, such as selling positions, private transportation of prohibited goods, and other misdeeds. Father Ki Talks About His Impressions of Traveling in Europe and India

The North-China Daily News reported that Father Ki, director of meteorology and seismology at the Xujiahui Observatory, recently traveled in Europe and has returned to Shanghai. Yesterday (the 9th), he discussed the results of this trip with a reporter from the North-China Daily News. He stated that he had three tasks for this trip: First, to attend the International Congress of Soil Science held in Lisbon, Portugal from September 17th to 24th. He presented three papers on earthquakes at the conference and also participated in the meteorological and geodetic sections of the conference. Second, to attend the International Maritime Meteorological Conference held in Utrecht, Netherlands, where he accomplished several important tasks. He proposed adding new signals for reporting severe weather during the day when hurricanes move along the Chinese coast. This new signal was proposed at the request of the new climate warning office that the Xujiahui Observatory will be opening. This office was requested by the Chinese government's Ministry of Industry to facilitate Chinese fishermen. Other observatories along the coasts of China and Vietnam naturally agreed. However, this new signal will only be used north of Hong Kong, as the low pressure systems that Shanghai often experiences are rare in Hong Kong and Vietnam. Third, to visit many climate and aviation offices in Europe to improve the affairs of the Xujiahui Observatory upon his return.

Economic Credit Cooperative Opens This Morning – Reception for Reporters Yesterday – General Manager Qiu Hanping Reports on Background and Benefits

The China Economic Credit Cooperative, initiated by Zhang Shouyong, Qiu Hanping, and others, is scheduled to open at 10 am today. Last night, the cooperative's chairman Zhang Shouyong, general manager Qiu Hanping, and others hosted a reception for the press at the Weiya Restaurant. During the reception, Mr. Qiu Hanping reported on the social background of the cooperative's establishment, the benefits of joining, and the reasons for the high profits. The main points are recorded below.

Background of Establishment

Since the Opium War, the import of goods by the great powers has completely collapsed China's inherent production system. At the same time, China's emerging industries have been unable to develop due to their oppression, leading to rural bankruptcy, unemployment, and unbearable suffering for the people. Coping with daily life has become difficult, and intellectuals are suffering from unemployment. Even if they can find a job, they are often unemployed the next day, and it is even more difficult to bear the burden of their families. They are constantly worried about their children's education during their lifetime and the lives of their wives and children after their death. They have no time to consider their spiritual lives. Seeing the suffering of the people today, we are eager to find a way to alleviate it, hence the establishment of this cooperative.

Membership Procedures

The membership procedures are very simple. Fill out a membership application form and pay a membership fee of one yuan, which is no different from ordinary social groups. The difference is that members must save a certain amount each month. This monthly saving is the basic obligation of the members. Members must fulfill this obligation to enjoy all rights. The monthly savings for a full share of the fifteen-year term (reaching [missing character] thousand yuan) is only five yuan, saving only seventeen cents a day to subscribe to a full share. There are also one-fifth and three-fifths shares. Those who can save two cents and three cents or ten cents a day can subscribe to one yuan or three yuan per month. There are also five-year and ten-year options to shorten the time. If you save all at once, the procedures are even simpler. The number of shares subscribed can also be increased according to the economic capacity of the subscriber. However, the maximum number of shares that each person can save is limited to five.

Benefits of Membership

After joining the cooperative, members have appropriate relief measures for everything from consumption and entertainment to temporary needs, from unemployment and illness to old-age care, and from children's education to their afterlife. Joining this cooperative is equivalent to having a guarantee for life-long life, and important life issues are resolved unexpectedly.

Reasons for High Profits

Perhaps there are those who doubt why the cooperative can give its members so many benefits that are not available in ordinary savings insurance. I do not know why the cooperative can give its members so many benefits, the reason is very obvious. First, the purpose of cooperation is to enable members to help themselves and each other. Second, it seeks the direct benefits of members and does not seek benefits for itself. In recent years, savings banks and insurance companies in Shanghai have developed very rapidly and have made great profits. What they pay in compensation is nothing more than using the mutual assistance of the insured, and what they pay in interest dividends is nothing more than using the funds of the savers. Going to save the small change into a bank, the interest earned is minimal. The bank collects this small change, or lends it or invests it, and earns huge profits in one transaction. The nature of cooperatives is different from ordinary banks and companies. They do not seek the interests of themselves and the dividends of shareholders, but seek the direct interests of members. All the interests of the shareholders of savings banks and life insurance companies are attributed to the members themselves. Therefore, the benefits enjoyed by the members are far beyond what ordinary insurance savings can provide. In addition, various entertainment facilities, medical and sports consultants, legal enrollment travel guidance, in the personal economic capacity, can not be done one by one, in the cooperative, it gathers the power of thousands of members to operate it, then the number of personal burden, is negligible, and is not perceived at all.

Communist Party Assassination Squad Key Suspects Transferred for Trial Pending – Each Suspect Also Committed Major Crimes Within the Concession – Transfer to the Public Safety Bureau Must Await Interrogation and Judgment

Cantonese Ouyang Zhiguang, Shanxi native Zhang Yushan, Chongming native Yuan Youfang, Cantonese Zhang Dexin, his wife Zhang Chenshi, Xuzhou native Dong Jiquan, Siyang native Cheng Xiangping (also known as Chen Xiangping), were key members of the Communist Party. They organized a "Dog Beating Squad" [slang for hunting traitors], their sole mission being to assassinate Communist Party traitors serving central government agencies. Countless public officials were assassinated by them. Due to their tight organization and swift methods, despite the best efforts of the police, their secrets could not be uncovered. Recently, detectives from the Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau Inspectorate suddenly obtained a lead and, on the 6th of this month, apprehended Cheng Xiangping at the Central Hotel in Xiaodongmen. Under rigorous interrogation, Cheng confessed that Ouyang and the other suspects were hiding at No. 33 Zhongxing Hotel on Hankou Road, No. 40 Longmen Road, and No. 88 Zaideri on North Chengdu Road, all within the Public Concession. Consequently, they cooperated with Chinese and Western detectives from the Lao Zha Police Station and went to the addresses to arrest Ouyang and the other six. Seven handguns, four Mauser pistols, three toxic gas pistols, and over one thousand rounds of ammunition were seized. They were handed over to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Because the police station still needed to inspect the handguns, the Public Safety Bureau's request for transfer was not granted. Details of this were previously reported in this newspaper. Now, the police station has discovered that the murder of Huang Yonghua, director of the Special Affairs Section of the Public Safety Bureau Inspectorate, and his follower Qian Yongqing, at the New World Company, the assassination of Central Special Commissioner Ma Shaowu in the garden, and the assault on two Public Safety Bureau secret agents at Siwenli on Xin Zha Road, among over ten other cases, were all committed by them. As the crimes all took place within the Public Concession, the police station decided to handle the cases. Consequently, Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Legal Department of the Public Works Department, filed a public prosecution with the Second Branch of the High Court. For the time being, the only case being prosecuted is the Huang Yonghua case. Yesterday morning, Yu Hua, the head of the Criminal Division of the High Court, along with assessors Zhao and Zhou, held a continued trial in Criminal Court One. The Public Safety Bureau was also represented by its legal advisor, lawyer Zhan Jifeng. The defendants also retained lawyers such as Zhang Ding to represent them. Judge Yu began by stating that the Public Safety Bureau had initially requested the transfer of the case, and therefore this issue should be resolved first. Lawyer Zhan immediately stated that the defendants were apprehended based on Cheng Xiangping's confession, and therefore requested their transfer. Police lawyer Li stated that the Public Works Department had initially agreed to the transfer, but after discovering major crimes committed within the Concession, it was now arguing that the High Court should first try the cases within the Concession before transferring them. Lawyer Zhan then stated that since the defendants had committed major crimes in the Concession, the High Court could proceed with those cases first, but the Public Safety Bureau still needed to investigate their headquarters. The defendants' lawyers also expressed opposition to the transfer. After deliberation, the court ruled that the police station had already filed charges against the defendants, and the transfer would be considered after the trial was concluded. After the ruling, police lawyer Li stated that Cheng Xiangping was also implicated in the crimes within the Concession and asked if the Public Safety Bureau could be ordered to hand her over for prosecution as well. Lawyer Zhan stated that if Cheng was indeed involved, the police station could discuss the matter with the Public Safety Bureau, and it would certainly be possible to hand her over. The court considered the transfer issue to be resolved, but as the defendants were not all present, proceedings could not continue and adjourned the trial for two weeks.

Infant Suffocated While Breastfeeding – Whether Liu Tangshi Was Negligent Still Under Investigation

Tang Bonian, a native of Hunan, 37 years old, is currently a secretary in the Finance Bureau of Beiping Municipality. His family resides at No. 219 Rue Sapore in the French Concession, Shanghai. His wife, née Yang, is of the same age and also from Hunan. They have lived in Shanghai and had four children, two of whom died young. On the 12th of last month, they had their fifth child, a boy named Youzhi. Because the mother was ill, they hired Liu Tangshi, a young woman from Yangzhou (21 years old), as a wet nurse. Only after a doctor certified that her milk was suitable was she hired at a monthly wage of nine yuan. At the beginning of her employment, Tangshi took care of the child diligently and cautiously, earning the deep appreciation of the master, who paid her four months' wages in advance. Unexpectedly, after receiving her wages, Tangshi's service gradually became indifferent. She paid no attention to the child's feeding times and often disobeyed the master's wishes, causing the master deep concern. However, because she had already been paid four months' wages and because she was physically strong, the master was reluctant to dismiss her. Therefore, the child slept with her grandmother, Tang Shenshi, every night, and Tangshi was only allowed to feed the child every two hours, day and night, to prevent accidents. Unexpectedly, at 11 a.m. on the night of the 9th, Tangshi was asleep when Tang's grandmother woke her up and handed her the child to feed. The grandmother went downstairs to eat congee. About fifty minutes later, after finishing her meal, she was about to take the child back from Tangshi to sleep together when she discovered that Tangshi was already fast asleep and that the child had been suffocated by her breast. When questioned, Tangshi refused to admit fault. She was immediately reported to the French police station, who dispatched detectives to arrest her. The child's body was taken to the Tongren Fu Yuan Joint Tang autopsy room. Yesterday, the Second Special District Local Court was notified, and the prosecutor arrived to examine the body. After examining the corpse and questioning the relatives, Tang Shenshi, and the accused, Liu Tangshi, the court ruled that the infant Tang Youzhi died of suffocation before death. The body was handed over to the relatives, Tang Shenshi, for burial. Whether the defendant Liu Tangshi was negligent in breastfeeding or caused the death of the child should be investigated and tried by the police department.

Woman Murdered in a Small Inn – A Large Man and an Old Man – Are the Murderers in This Case

At 7:15 last night, a woman was murdered in a small inn on Rue Hennequin in the French Concession. The two murderers escaped without a trace. The following is a record of the events that transpired.

Large Man Rents a Room

A large man suddenly arrived at the Rong'an Inn at No. 34 Rue Hennequin in the French Concession. He claimed to be Shen A'er, 38 years old, a local. He rented Room No. 5, a pavilion room on the third floor, paying six jiao, small silver coins, for one night's room fee. After completing the transaction, the large man hurriedly left again.

Tragedy Occurs in a Blink

After leaving, the large man returned fifteen minutes later, leading an old man and a middle-aged woman in tattered clothes. Shen claimed that the woman, née He, was 40 years old. The three entered the room. The tea boy made tea and then went downstairs. Since there were three people, he did not suspect anything. But unexpectedly, a tragedy occurred in a blink of an eye.

Two Men Leave One After Another

About half an hour after the tea boy went downstairs, the old man left first, followed by Shen a few minutes later. No one paid attention at the time. After a long time, the two did not return. Then the tea boy, Wang A'ru (36 years old, from Ningbo), went upstairs on business. When he passed Room No. 5 in the pavilion, he saw no movement inside the room, and the door was half open, not bolted. So he pushed the door open.

Woman Already Tragically Dead

When tea boy Wang A'ru pushed open the door, he saw the curtains were drawn and there was no response when he called out. Sensing something was wrong, he lifted the curtains and suddenly saw the woman who had entered the room earlier lying face up on the bed, the bedclothes covered in blood, her hands and feet tightly bound with hemp rope, and a knife inserted in her throat. Feeling her, he found that she was already dead. The tea boy was terrified and rushed to tell the innkeeper, Wang Mao Mao, who reported it to the police station. The head of the police station immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. The body was carried to the Tongren Fu Yuan Hall autopsy room, and the Second Special District was notified for examination.

Lieutenant Hall Sentenced – Sentenced to Two Years and Six Months in Prison

According to the American Evening Post, American aviator Lieutenant Hall was sentenced to two years and six months in prison this morning (the 10th) by American Judge Pandy for defrauding General He Guoguo of 9,775 yuan intended for purchasing handguns. It is reported that when the trial began last Friday, Hall admitted his guilt but claimed that the money was given to a German arms dealer who was a private merchant and he had a receipt at the time. He also stated that the receipt and other documents were detained by Japanese authorities when he was arrested in Moji. However, after the American court asked the American Consul in Kobe to investigate, the Japanese authorities denied detaining any documents. When the trial was reopened today, Hall again admitted that his previous statement about the woman he sent back to the United States being his wife was also a lie, but she was actually his mistress. He gave her 1,240 gold yuan. The two had lived together in China for eighteen months. When he ran out of money, he defrauded General He of the money and sent her back to the United States. Now that the American Judge Pandy has concluded the case, he will go to Hong Kong on the President Taft steamer tomorrow with his clerk, Collin, to open cases in Guangzhou. However, it is heard that there are no major cases in southern China. Judge Pandy and others can still return to Shanghai on the original ship.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Supervising New Ship Commissioners Wu Daming and Shi Gan Scheduled to Sail – Will Leave Shanghai on the 18th of This Month

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company borrowed 400,000 pounds from the British Boxer Indemnity to order four ocean-going vessels from the United Kingdom. The contract has already been sent to the Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors and mailed to London. As the construction of the new vessels has begun in England, the supervising commissioners dispatched by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will be sailing from Shanghai soon. The details are as follows:

Four New Vessels Being Built in England

The four new ocean-going vessels built with the Boxer Indemnity funds are designated to run the South China route. Each vessel costs approximately 1.05 million yuan. The specifications regarding the tonnage, dimensions, and deck layout have been drawn up by the company and sent to the Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors and then to London, where the British Boxer Indemnity Commission is commissioning them according to the specifications. The deadline is tight. The vessels must be delivered within one year at most for deployment on the South China route.

Materials for Two Vessels Purchased in England

As for the two Yangtze River vessels, because they cannot cross the ocean to China, the policy has been changed to purchase materials in the United Kingdom and ship them to Shanghai, where the hull will be built by the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory in this port. The machinery and other components inside the vessels will all be British goods and will be shipped to Shanghai for assembly. All taxes on the machinery for the two Yangtze River vessels are paid by the company and are not included in the purchase price.

Commissioners Complete Their Affairs

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to appoint Wu Daming, a section chief of the Ministry of Communications, and Shi Gan, an advisor within the company, as commissioners to supervise the construction of the new vessels in England. The request was approved by the Ministry of Communications, and their salaries and expenses were stipulated. However, due to unfinished duties, Wu and Shi postponed their departure. Now, Wu and Shi have completed all their affairs and come to Shanghai to prepare for their departure.

Scheduled to Go to England to Build Ships

As the new vessels in London are already under construction, supervising commissioners Wu and Shi urgently need to depart to monitor them. Shi Gan has already arrived at the company yesterday to discuss the departure procedures. Wu Daming is also packing his luggage and preparing to receive his travel expense certificate for traveling abroad. It has been confirmed that Wu and Shi have decided to leave Shanghai for London on the British ship Edina on the 18th of this month to take on the duties of supervising the construction of the new ships.

National Medical Association to Hold Third National Congress – Date… January 1st to 3rd Next Year – Venue… Nanjing YMCA, Zhonghua Road, Nanjing

The National Medical Association will convene its Third National Congress on New Year's Day next year. The venue is said to have been decided as the Nanjing YMCA on Zhonghua Road, Nanjing. The congress is scheduled from January 1st to 3rd next year. Exhibition rooms will be added inside and outside the venue to display medicines for various pharmaceutical factories and pharmacies from different regions. To facilitate contact with pharmaceutical factories, the association has entrusted Pan Ruitang of Jicheng Pharmacy at No. 166 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, as the exhibition director for this congress to be responsible for organizing the exhibition. Last week, the association's secretary, Zhu Shanji, accompanied Mr. Pan to Beijing to measure the diagrams of the congress venue and exhibition rooms. They have now returned to Shanghai, and the diagrams will be fully distributed to the pharmaceutical factories next Monday to allow them to secure places quickly. The association's draft letter to the medical associations is copied below. Sirs, This is to inform you that the date of the Association's Third Congress is set to convene from January 1st to 3rd, the first three days of the New Year, to be held at the Nanjing YMCA on Zhonghua Road in Nanjing. We especially send this letter to inform you that we would like your association to follow Article 10 of Chapter 5 of the Association's Constitution and immediately nominate representatives to attend. In addition, if your association has any proposals for the congress, please send them two weeks before the congress so that they can be reviewed and arranged.
