Free Talk

"Negotiated" Literary Giants

— Bai Zaixuan

The tip of the pen is also sharp and must penetrate. If it cannot penetrate elsewhere, it can only exaggerate the advertisements in literary magazines and stab them.

Looking at the magazine's advertisements, every author is a literary giant. It seems that the Chinese literary scene is so bright and magnificent. However,

It also attracts snorts from the nostrils. However, writers who write for a lifetime and hide their names in famous mountains, waiting for archaeological teams to excavate them, no longer exist. Even poets who write and carve their own works into a thin book and distribute it to friends are rarely encountered. Now, manuscripts are written one week, published the next week, clipped and pasted last month, and published next month, mostly just for稿費. If we say that the authors are starving and dedicated to serving society, I am afraid that it would be a bit embarrassing to say, even the noble person who laughs at people needing稿費 still cannot avoid needing稿費 for his mocking article. But of course, literary giants who have other salaries or can rely on women's dowries to support them do not belong to this category.

Generally speaking, the root is in selling money, so the various literary giants in Shanghai have been "negotiated" for a long time.

After the merchant prints a manuscript, if feudalism is in power at that time, the advertisement will say that the author is a feudal literary giant. When the revolution is in progress, he will be a revolutionary literary giant. Thus, a group of literary giants is sealed. If another company's book is also printed, another advertisement will say that the author is not a real feudal or revolutionary literary giant, but that this side's is the real thing. Thus, another group of literary giants is sealed. Another company gathers and prints various argumentative advertisements. An author adds some criticism, and another new literary giant emerges.

Another method is to combine a set of characters, ask a few poets, a few novelists, and a critic to discuss and establish some kind of society. When the advertisement is published, they overthrow the existing literary giants and promote new literary giants. As a result, a group of literary giants can always be sealed, which is also a kind of "negotiation".

Generally speaking, the root is selling money, so the later book prices will inevitably point out the true value of the literary giants, priced at two catties for one, or five cents a pile, which is also uncertain. However, there is one exception: when a store clears out its inventory and sells its works cheaply, it is not because the literary giants have reached the end of the road, but because they have already "climbed up" and entered universities and government offices, and no longer need this stepping stone.

China as Seen by Americans

— Yao Ke

In recent years, sales of books and newspapers about China in the American publishing world have shown a considerable surge. Pearl Buck's "The Good Earth," needless to say, had already "spread without needing to be pushed," earning world renown. Considering only the books published this year, there are too many about China to read them all. From what I have personally seen, there are two books that are very worthy of our attention, and from which we can understand what "China as Seen by Americans" is all about.

One is "Far Eastern Front," published in September of this year. The author, Edgar Snow, is a Far East correspondent for an American news agency. In this 336-page book, he starkly exposes the entire Far Eastern situation. The "aggressor nation's" conspiracy to annex the Northeast, the process of the loss of the three Northeastern provinces, the inside story of "non-resistance," the sketches of the Battle of Shanghai and the establishment of the puppet state, the fall of Jehol and the meaning of the Tanggu Truce—all unfold like a movie in this book. The subtlety and thoroughness of his observations, the vividness and accuracy of his writing style, and the fairness and incisiveness of his argumentation are truly astonishing. But what moved me most were the chapters on the Chinese people and the political status quo, and the inferences about the future of the Far East situation. The author says on page 326: "Over the years, names, governments, and plans have changed, but the play on stage remains the same. All kinds of bad elements and qualities seem to continue endlessly—lacking meaning, unity, and scientific action." This is China as seen by Americans—although very disappointing, we cannot find any evidence to refute this view. Facts speak louder than words; even if we argue, it would only be like "taking off our pants to cover our face," making us look even more shameful.

There are many more pertinent and poignant words, and I originally wanted to translate a few sentences, but due to lack of free time, I can only let readers find the original book themselves.

Another book is the novel "The House of Exile" by female writer Nora Waln. This book was published in April of this year and has been reprinted eight times in just three months, and is said to be the best-selling novel in the United States this year. However, the story in the book is not only ordinary but also dull, and the absurdities in it are too numerous to list. For example: a woman who gets married in November gives birth to a son by February of the following year, and there is no description or possibility of her and her fiancé "trading beforehand"; Cai Tingkai of the Nineteenth Route Army has become a nationally renowned "dreamy young poet"; a Chinese family with six generations living under one roof can trace its genealogy to more than 139 generations. Even the "Duke Yansheng" of our Shandong is only the 77th generation descendant of Confucius—we can laugh at these absurdities. However, there are many fallacies about politics and society in it that cannot be tolerated. For example, she said that China had already begun to fiercely boycott Japanese goods in the spring of 1931, but in fact, it was not until after the Wanbaoshan Incident on July 2 that there was a boycott movement. As for the depiction of Chinese life, it is even more absurd and gives American readers a very erroneous impression.

What is most annoying is the author's own standpoint. Although this book is called a novel, it is actually written in the tone of an "eyewitness" autobiography. American readers who have never been to China can easily mistake it for the truth, which is what we expected. What's more, Pearl Buck praised it, saying, "There is no question about the authenticity of this book." This is another unpleasant book.

The above two books give me two different kinds of unpleasantness. The first is the unpleasantness of—as Oscar Wilde once said—"Caliban seeing his true face in the mirror," and the second is the unpleasantness of "Caliban not seeing his true face in the mirror." "Far Eastern Front," in my opinion, is the most faithful and sharp in its observations of the Sino-Japanese conflict and the current situation in China, and its argumentation is the most insightful and fair, but it inevitably shows us our ugliness. For me, it's just a little unpleasant, but wealthy people may be (unable?) to laugh or cry after reading it. As for the book "The House of Exile," unless we want to find some laughs, we might as well not read it; but I think the Chinese PEN might as well send some comments to the United States to correct this erroneous impression, so as to avoid the joke of American poets asking Cai Tingkai to write couplets in the future.

Villagers

— Cheng Yunping

Everyone's hearts were filled with suspicion, and a little panic. It wasn't unusual for a monk seeking alms to come to the village. But in these years of war and chaos, even a slight deviation from the ordinary, like someone shouting a few times in the middle of the night, could make the villagers jump out of bed and run barefoot outside. With the arrival of the monk, everyone suspected that he was a spy, sent by bandits to scout whether there were any troops stationed there. The monk was a strong man in his thirties, and everyone said that if he hadn't been sent by the bandits, how could he be so physically strong? As he walked along the road, he kept knocking on his wooden fish and looking around, which was further proof that he had ulterior motives. The monk was staying in the Guandi Temple at the head of the village. So, a large group of people went to investigate.

The moonlight wasn't very bright, and the wind rustled through the grass. The group of people discussed in hushed tones on the road. Some advocated stopping him and sending him to the city tomorrow, while others advocated getting rid of him tonight, lest he harm our village. Everyone tiptoed, trying not to let him know, so that they could see what he was doing there.

Peeking through the crack in the door, the monk was unexpectedly calmly sitting in meditation and chanting scriptures. So, everyone rushed in like a swarm of bees. The monk greeted everyone very politely.

"Where did you come from, Master?" the leader asked directly.

"Hunan XX Mountain. What brings you all here?" the monk replied very respectfully.

"Please leave this place!"

"These days, it's not good for strangers to stay!" everyone shouted along.

The monk asked to leave early the next morning. However, everyone refused to allow it. Everyone clamored and shouted. The monk helplessly packed his luggage and left in the night. But everyone was still suspicious, afraid that he might come back tonight and that something might happen. Even the children couldn't sleep soundly. They were filled with suspicion and panic until daybreak.

The Human World

— Liao Botan

So tired, so thirsty! Sweat! Sweat rolling down.

My hat is dripping. This deadly hot summer!

I rested in XX Park.

The men carrying shoulder poles groaned; the trees drooped their heads lazily...

The world seemed exhausted! But they had to call out, to groan.

Flies, bees, "mosquitoes," flying here, buzzing there, truly busy.

From outside came the clanging sound of a blind fortune-teller, slowly, bringing a touch of serenity.

From that side, a gray friend came walking, with a broken leg and an injured hand, and sat down beside me.

His face, paper-white and tinged with gray-black; one hand bandaged and hanging; a wooden crutch replacing his foot.

Standing at the edge of the world, this poor man! I thought.

"Ah!" he sighed; his eyes drooped, lazy; after a moment, he raised his face, now nothing but skin and bones, looked at the sky; then, immediately, he lowered it again.

Is this a human being?

丨At least there's a skeleton here, even skeletons are gone beneath the Jizhong Pagoda! Who was saying that, I don't know.

I glanced at him sideways, he was weeping.

He was weeping, and I was weeping too, why?

Looking more closely, a photo of an old woman, fifty or sixty years old, was spinning in his hand!

The Two Brothers (25)

— By Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

Then he suddenly sat down again. He didn't like her, this woman! Why? She belonged to the kind of ordinary and base considerations; and besides, wasn't she comparatively fond of Zhean? Although he himself didn't explicitly admit it, most of the reason why he didn't think much of this widow was because she preferred Zhean, because although he liked his younger brother, he always thought he was a bit mediocre, while he himself was comparatively superior.

In any case, he couldn't sit here until evening; so, like the previous evening, he anxiously wondered: "What should I do?"

He now felt that his heart needed to be moved, needed someone to embrace him, to comfort him. What exactly did he need comforting for? He himself couldn't say for sure, but he was now feeling weak and tired; at this time, the appearance of a woman, a woman's comfort, the touch of a slender hand, the rustling of a woman's dress, a black or blue tender look in the eyes, seemed to be what our hearts urgently demanded, absolutely essential.

He now remembered a young waitress in a beer hall who had taken him home to sleep one night and whom he had often seen since then.

So he stood up again, preparing to go and have a beer with this girl. What was he going to say to her? What would he say to her? Undoubtedly, nothing at all. But what did that matter? He could hold her hand for a while. She seemed to like him. Why hadn't he gone to see her more often?

When he arrived, she was sitting on a chair dozing off in the almost empty beer hall. A customer was resting his arm on the oak table smoking a pipe, the woman in charge was reading a novel, and the owner of the beer hall was sound asleep on the wooden stool wearing only his undershirt.

The girl, as soon as she saw him, quickly stood up and walked over to him, saying:

"Good morning, how are you?"

"Not bad, and you?"

"Me, I'm great. You rarely come, do you?"

"Yeah, I simply can't find the time. You know I'm a doctor."

"Oh, you never told me that before. If I had known you were a doctor, I would have asked you to see me when I was sick last week. What do you want to drink?"

"A beer, and you?"

"Me, I'll also have a beer, anyway, you're paying for it."

She continued to talk to him in an intimate tone, as if him buying her a beer implicitly gave her this right. So the two sat down face to face and chatted. She often took his hand in an affectatious way that women who sell smiles easily have, and looked at him with an enticing gaze, saying to him:

"Why don't you come more often? Darling, I really like you."

But he was already getting tired of her, finding her stupid, ordinary, and smelling of the lower classes. He thought: women should appear in dreams or in a luxurious atmosphere that can poeticize their vulgarity.

She asked him:

"One morning you walked past with a handsome man with golden hair and a full beard, was that your brother?"

"Yes, that's my brother."

Financial Exchange Soars, Gold Price Drops Another $6.50; New Low of $727.50 Appears on the Market; Weakness in Futures Increases, Stable Process All Day

The gold market continued to decline yesterday, breaking the $30 mark. It remained stable after opening, but the outlook was still calm. In the morning, the overseas silver market showed rises in both the UK and US. The five-metal exchange showed a futures silver price increase of 2.5 to 4 points. Silk & Tea: Sudden Changes in the London Tea Market

London is an extremely large market for black tea sales. In recent years, due to the overproduction of Indian tin-lined safflower, tea prices have gradually fallen, and tea farmers and merchants have suffered from it. As a result of several restrictions on production by French, British and Dutch tea merchants, the backlog was finally cleared this spring, and Indian tin tea prices have gradually risen again. Due to the lower selling price of black tea in the two lakes of China than that of Indian tin tea, sales have been very active. According to statistics, no less than 80,000 boxes were imported into the United Kingdom this year, Qining black tea

The news that the experts got changed suddenly. Indian tin tea prices have plummeted. Except for high-quality Qimen goods, Chinese tea has not been much affected, and the rest are all stockpiled and not moving. The reason is that the deterioration of Russian-Japanese relations has completely stagnated the trade in Indian and Javanese tea with Russia.

Talk

"Fishing for the Moon in the Sea"

— of

To fish for the moon in the sea is to sink one's body to the bottom of the sea, and it is also something that cannot be caught. Because the moon is produced in the sky, and the sea is only a faint and empty shadow of it. Think about it. Can a faint and empty shadow be caught? Unless he's really a fool!

Although, but people always like to do this faint and empty sea-fishing moon business 丨丨 The more faint and empty and unpredictable, the more they like to do it, and the more crazy and universal they do it! In the past, I only heard that there were many poets and literati who drove a small boat on a still night with a bright moon and sparse stars, and went to the lake to drink wine and compose poems and write fu facing the moon (the moon in the moon). It is said that this is the most elegant thing, but in fact, it is at most a kind of plaything belonging to windiness and boredom. Although they are only humming in their mouths, expressing appreciation and praise for this faint and empty moon in the water, after all, they have not taken off their socks, rolled up their trousers, and gone into the water to fish, so they still belong to the "literary" school after all.

However, the "moon in the water" will not be easily let go once it reaches the hands of non-literati or appears in front of non-literati. They always have to automatically or passively use their simple and ridiculous brains to think of unconventional methods, that is, to strip naked or even peel off their skin and draw out their tendons, they are also willing to go into the water to fish. But what is the result? How much and what do they catch after all? In addition to illusion, emptiness, curses, depression, and nakedness, exposure, peeling, tendon drawing, etc., will there be any other slightly practical significance?

In all the markets today, there are many clever gentlemen who are used to teasing people and taking advantage of them, and they secretly hang up a mirror-like thing that dazzles people's eyes or stimulates people's hearts, and emits a fierce and terrifying strong light, which shines on the rivers and seas, so that the rivers and seas also reflect a faint and empty shadow that is similar to having a child. A group of dull-headed fools and idiots will throw away their existing clothes and socks, endure the pain of skin and tendons, and jump into the sea to fish. When the fools and idiots are groping in the water, the always bright gentlemen who are playing tricks on the shore in the dark will collect their Dharma, roll up the clothes and socks of the fools and idiots, and take their skins and tendons to their own warm rooms, laughing and having fun! At this time, some of the fools in the sea realized that this was an unpredictable illusion and emptiness, so they resolutely climbed ashore, naked and covered with scars, and went home to make clothes, socks, rest, and heal injuries; some still lay in the water, cultivating their energy and waiting, waiting for the next time the moon appears so that they can fish again, even if they fish themselves to annihilation, they will not give up, he said: "I will fish for this moon even if I become a ghost."

Some people say: The fool is willing to give up everything and go into the sea to fish for this unpredictable, illusory, and empty moon, which shows his foolishness, dullness, stupidity, and abnormality 丨 But he still has consciousness, when he looks at the moon in the sea, accidentally, he will definitely look up and see the real moon in the sky. At this time, it is only because the moon in the sky is too far away from him, and it is too laborious and difficult to obtain, and the moon on the sea in front of him, he does not know is false, he thinks it seems that he can get it easily without much effort, so he abandons the far and takes the near, avoiding the heavy and doing dull things, resulting in the destruction of the whole self 丨 Therefore, their motives are still laziness, greed, and rascality! ……

Yes, but. We are essential, and we always have to actually obtain it. However, to actually obtain it, it is necessary to smash all the mirrors and magic weapons that create unpredictable, illusory, and empty fake moons, as well as all kinds of smoke screens. We will use the courage and determination to jump into the sea to obtain the real moon in the sky that is farther away from us, and must go through effort and difficulty before we can get it!

If you really want the moon, go to the sky to get it 丨

Servant

— Ryoka

Among human beings today, the most pitiful are servants, and the most hateful are also servants. This is caused by their special environment. It seems that it should not be harsh to blame them themselves. Here I just want to make a review of their special environment.

Everyone knows that two groups of five out of ten servants are proletarians. In this way, in the basis of human life, they can only be ranked on the dangerous minimum front. In fact, many simple people are living an extremely low life, as if they are similar to beggars patrolling along the door, and spiritually and in their souls, they must be tightened a lot.

However, after all, it is not like this. They have a lot of opportunities to connect with the rich, and they are a group with a lot of hope and vitality. This does not require historical research. Just flip through the stories. In the past 100 years, successful people who are "worthy of being passed down" are often used as teaching materials for the "civics" class in schools, and there are often amazing examples of such servants. For example: "So-and-so was born in poverty, and when he was thirty years old, he began to follow a wealthy Westerner to serve as a messenger. He was valued by his master for his loyalty and diligence. Later, his credit increased day by day, and his status became higher and higher. He stood on his own and his reputation suddenly rose. He was one of the great men of the time."

From this, it can be seen that the ability of servants to connect with the rich, to have hope, and to have vitality, all depends on loyalty and diligence. Loyalty and diligence are the only elixir for servants to rise high, so logically, all loyal and diligent servants have hope and vitality. Taking the facts before us as an example, loyal and diligent servants all gain the favor of their masters. As long as this is the case, the master will not hide any tricks or secrets from you, and some things even require you to come forward. When going out, in addition to taking a large male dog to protect them, it is also necessary for two or three servants to stand in front to boost their courage.

So, even more, from the current appearance of servants, their material enjoyment must also be very lively. Needless to say, ordinary errand girls, etc., wear, eat, and drink, most of them are somewhat like young wives and young masters, and their bodies are white and plump. The best is that the maids are holding little angels and driving a car alone on the road. We often encounter them. Of course, there are also quite a few who follow wealthy people and dignitaries to sit in flower cars to add color to the "comings and goings of crowns and canopies" in Beijing and Shanghai. Therefore, their comfortable life can be imagined.

The life of a servant is so lively and so guaranteed! It is because they are connected to wealthy people and dignitaries.

What is more, in addition to the importance of the master and the enjoyment bestowed by the master, there are often unexpected importance and rewards. For example, the young lady secretly communicates with wild men, and even secretly goes out on dates, which is very beneficial to the maids and the like. As long as they are loyal and reliable, the young lady is very trusting, and many major events will be sent to you, such as secretly delivering love letters and lightly getting up in the middle of the night to open the back door. In this way, the young lady will also take special care of you. In addition to putting on a good face and good feelings in front of you, in addition to giving you a lot of half-new and old clothes and stockings, in addition to having a small account for you, she will also speak on behalf of you in front of her mother and father to increase your salary. Similarly, the young master and the errand driver also have so many connections, such as being lazy in school and needing the maids to help them and massage their shoulders, and the rewards are not light.

Under these various circumstances, these servants are very arrogant to a group of people, and even act like a tiger and act as an accomplice. Therefore, many people now say that the world is too unlike what it should be and must be reformed. The servants do not think so much, which is precisely because they have the various relationships mentioned above, and they are tightly clinging to the "anesthetic." Therefore, they are not only very unbelieving, but also can give birth to powerful reactions, baring their teeth and claws, which is extremely fierce. When they once "prosper", their efforts to oppress and exploit those below will be deeper and more severe. Servants have lost some souls and awareness.

Therefore, in mankind, the most pitiful are servants, and the most hateful are also servants.

Page 23

Women

— Jing Jia

"I need a woman." Ping told me in his letter: "I'm too lonely, I'm lonely like"

"Like a stone statue in the desert. No one to comfort me, to make me happy. I need a woman! Without a woman, emptiness will swallow me."

After reading the letter, I found it quite funny. I remembered his lanky figure, disheveled hair, flat nose, wide mouth, and that face covered in freckles.

Ping is a clerk at XX Company. The company isn't far from my house. I made a phone call to him, and I said: "I hope you can come to my house to talk."

That night, heavy raindrops beat on the ground. It was early summer weather. Very stuffy. Even such heavy rain couldn't wash away the sultriness.

I sat alone, reading Mao Dun's works. I heard the door open. Looking up, I saw a drenched chicken, which was the pitiful Ping.

"You need a woman?" I asked bluntly.

"What? Shouldn't I have one?"

"You should indeed!" I said, "You're grown up, and you have a job. Unlike me, who spends my life grinding away in books and classrooms."

"I think I should have one!" Ping lit a cigarette. "You really don't know how lonely I am!"

After a moment of silence, Ping said, "When I see those couples walking down the street with their arms around each other, I hate it: no, it's not hate, it's jealousy, I can assure you. I blush and sweat when I see women. But this time I should muster some courage!"

"I believe you already have someone in mind."

"No," he said, "I don't."

"You're not honest, your eyes have already told me!"

"Really? You really are a keen observer!" Ping blew smoke in my face. "Ha, I really do have someone!"

"Is that so!" I said, suppressing a smile, "You're so lucky in love! Can you tell me more details?"

"She's my classmate!" Ping said.

"Have you been to the movies together?"

"Go to the movies! How relaxed! We haven't even started writing our names in the register yet!"

"Doesn't she love you?"

"I don't know, I only know that I love her!"

"Haha!" I laughed, "What a ridiculous thing!"

"What? Can't I love her?" Ping was a bit angry!

"Not at all! Don't misunderstand. What do you want to do?" He scratched his head and threw the cigarette butt into the spittoon. "I must launch an attack. She really is breathtakingly beautiful! I think about her every moment."

So I asked, "How do you want to attack?"

He lit his second cigarette, paused for a moment, and said, "I want to write a letter, do you think that's a good idea?"

"Of course!" I said, "Writing a letter is a good idea, but it's hard to write one that's touching."

"It doesn't matter, I'll do my best to write it."

"I wish you victory!"

Ping didn't reply, he lay back in the chair, tilted his head back, and rings of blue smoke puffed out of his mouth, disappearing little by little!

I moved my chair, I stroked his disheveled hair with my hand: "You should first put some oil in your hair, and you should also apply some powder to your face."

Ping smiled and said, "That's true."

So I said teasingly, "Is it possible to tell me the lady's name?"

"I can't!"

"You'll have to tell me eventually anyway." I said, "Isn't it the same now?"

"Her surname is Yin." Ping said.

"Surname Yin?" I exclaimed in surprise. "What's her given name?"

"Lixia."

"Yin Lixia, Yin Lixia! Haha!" I laughed wildly!

"Hey, what's so funny!"

"Ha!" I tried my best to suppress my laughter. "That really is a beautiful name!"

"This is really a ridiculous thing!" I thought.

After a while, Ping got up to leave, and before leaving, he also firmly said: "Tonight, I must begin my work."

After Ping left, I lay in bed and thought quietly for half an hour. So I decided to proceed with my plan.

(II)

A week later, Ping wrote to report his progress: "I've already received her reply. She has literary talent. It really is a touching love letter! I almost suspect I'm dreaming."

I wrote a line of words on red paper for him, I said: "Congratulations on your victory, reserve a banquet seat in advance."

Three days later, Ping made a phone call to me, he said: "Tomorrow we're going to XX Grand Theater."

"Her?" I asked.

"Of course, she's going too."

"What about me?"

"No admittance."

"That won't do."

"It's inconvenient."

"I don't care."

"I'm sorry, don't make trouble."

"Can you stop me from watching the play?"

"Fine, go yourself. I don't care."

The phone hung up, and I laughed so hard I almost fell over.

The next afternoon. I arrived at XX Grand Theater. It was already quite late, the downstairs was already full! I went upstairs, and in the corner on the right I spotted Ping. I saw him wearing a very stiff suit, his hair also slicked with oil, and the freckles on his face were also partially concealed by snow powder and the like. From the time I met him until now, it was the first time I had seen him so neat.

When he saw me, he was very awkward. He greeted me.

I walked to the row where he was sitting. The lady Ping admired, who was sitting next to him, stood up and nodded to me, she said: "You're just arriving!"

I said with a smile: "I thought it was still too early!"

Ping said in surprise: "Do you know Ms. Yin?"

I gently sat down on the empty seat next to him, I gently stroked Ping's hair, I looked at the floorboards, I said softly: "She is my fiancée."
